Pledgee's Right to Retain Pledge Until Full Repayment
Ruling with proof establishing pledgee's retention right and analogical extension to partial payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the pledgee's right of retention (habs) over the pledge until full debt payment, and explain the ruling when partial payment is made or the pledge perishes after full payment.

Core Idea
Partial payment does not release a proportionate part of the pledge; the pledgee retains the whole until full payment.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar establishes a fundamental principle in Hanafi pledge law: the pledgee's right to retain the entire pledge as security until the debt is fully satisfied. Even if the pledgor makes a partial payment, the pledgee may keep the whole pledge, analogizing to the seller's retention of the sold item until full price is paid. The passage also addresses two further issues: the obligation to surrender upon full payment, and the return of payment if the pledge perishes after full payment but before surrender to avoid double recovery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule
The pledgee is not obliged to allow sale or surrender of the pledge until the debt is fully paid. This is due to the perpetual retention nature of a pledge.
2
Analyze the analogy to sale
The text draws a qiyas jaliyy (clear analogy) between the pledgee's retention and the seller's retention of the sold item (mabi') until full payment. Identify the asl (sale) and far' (pledge).
The illa (effective cause) is the existence of unpaid debt.
3
Apply partial payment scenario
Understand that partial payment does not entitle the pledgor to release a portion; the pledgee retains the entire pledge by analogy.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: other schools might differ.
4
Determine the ruling after full payment
Upon full payment, the obstacle (debt) is removed, and the pledgee must surrender the pledge.
The right of retention ceases.
5
Handle post-payment destruction
If the pledge perishes after full payment but before surrender, the pledgor recovers the paid amount because the pledge's value already satisfied the debt, preventing double recovery.
This ensures justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان كان الرهن فى يده ليس عليه ان يمكنه من البيع حتى يقضيه الدين لان حكمه الحبس الدائم الى ان يقضى الدين على ما بيناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر رہن مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہو تو مرتہن پر ضروری نہیں کہ وہ راہن کو مرہون فروخت کرنے کی قدرت دے یہاں تک کہ راہن اس کا قرض ادا کر دے اس لئے کہ رہن کا حکم حبس دائم ہی یہاں تک کہ راہن قرض ادا کر دے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم ( اوائل کتاب الرہن میں ) بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح جب تک مرتهن اپنا قرض وصول نہ کرے جب تک اس کو حق ہے کہ رہن واپس نہ کرے لہذا اگر راہن رہن کو فروخت کرنا چاہے تو مرتہن پر یہ ضروری نہیں کہ وہ رہن کو فروخت کرنے دے۔
مسائل ثلثہ کی وضاحت
ولو قضاه البعض فله ان يحبس كل الرهن حتى يستوفي البقية اعتبارا بحبس المبيع فاذا قضاه الدين قيل له سلم الرهن اليه لانه زال المانع من التسليم لوصول الحق الى مستحقه فلو هلک قبل التسلیم استرد الراهن ما قضاه لانه صار مستوفيا عند الهلاك بالقبض السابق فكان الثانى استيفاء بعد استيفاء فيجب رده ترجمہ اور اگر مرتین کو کچھ قرض ادا کر دیا تو مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ وہ پورا رہن روک نے یہاں تک کہ باقی کو وصول کرے جبس مبیع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے پس جب راہن نے مرتہن کو پورا قرض اداء کر دیا تو مرتہن سے کہا جائیگا کہ رہن راہن کے حوالہ کر اس لئے کہ جو چیز سپرد کرنے سے مانع تھی وہ زائل ہو گئی حق کے اس کے متحقق تک پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے پس اگر رہن ہلاک ہو گیا سپر د کرنے سے پہلے تو راہن وہ مال واپس لیگا جو مرتہن کو ادا کیا تھا اس لئے کہ مرتہن ہلاکت کے وقت سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے وصول کرنے والا ہو گیا تو دوسرا وصول کرنا وصول کرنے کے بعد وصول کرتا ہوگا پس اس کا ( ثانی کا ) واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں تین مسائل ہیں۔ ۱۔ باب بیچ میں بائع کو حق ہوتا ہے کہ جب تک مشتری شمن ادا نہ کرے صبیع حوالہ نہ کرے بلکہ اپنے پاس روکے رکھے اور اگر مشتری نے کچھ مشن ادا کر دیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تب بھی بائع کو حق ہے کہ پوراشن وصول کرنے تک مبیع کو روکے رکھے اسی طرح اگر راہن نے کچھ قرض ادا کر دیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تو مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ جب تک راہن پورا قرض ادا نہ کرے مرہون کورو کے رکھے۔ ۲۔ جب راہن نے پورا قرض ادا کر دیا تو اب مرتہن کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ مرہون کو اپنے پاس روکے رکھے کیونکہ مرتہن نے اپنا حق وصول کر لیا تو جس بنیاد پر مرتہن کو جس کا حکم تھا وہ بنیاد ختم ہوگئی۔ ۳۔ راہن نے پورا قرض ادا کر دیا اور اداء دین کے بعد اتفاق سے مرتہن کے پاس مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا تو راہن نے جو قرض ادا کیا تھا اس کو واپس لے گا کیونکہ مرتہن اس ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اپنا قرض وصول کرنے والا ہو گیا تو یہ ڈبل وصول ہو جائے گا اس سے بچنے کے لئے اس کی واپسی ضروری ہے۔
He said: And if the pledge is in his hand, he is not obliged to enable him to sell it until he pays the debt, because its ruling is perpetual retention until the debt is paid, as we have explained.
Translation: Quduri said: And if the pledge is in the possession of the pledgee, it is not necessary for the pledgee to give the pledgor the power to sell the pledge until the pledgor pays his debt, because the ruling of the pledge is perpetual retention until the pledgor pays the debt according to the detail we have (in the beginning of the Book of Pledge). Explanation: As long as the pledgee has not collected his debt, he has the right not to return the pledge. So if the pledgor wants to sell the pledge, the pledgee is not obliged to allow the sale.
Clarification of three issues: And if he pays part of the debt, he has the right to retain the entire pledge until he collects the remainder, by analogy to the retention of the sold item. Then when he pays the full debt, it is said to him: Surrender the pledge to him, because the obstacle to surrender has been removed due to the right reaching its rightful owner. So if it perishes before surrender, the pledgor recovers what he paid, because at the time of destruction, the pledgee becomes a collector by virtue of the prior possession, so the second collection would be collection after collection, so it must be returned.
Explanation: This passage contains three issues. 1. In the chapter of sale, the seller has the right not to surrender the sold item until the buyer pays the price; and if the buyer pays part and some remains, the seller still has the right to retain the entire sold item until full payment. Similarly, if the pledgor pays part of the debt and some remains, the pledgee has the right to retain the entire pledge until the pledgor pays the full debt. 2. When the pledgor pays the full debt, the pledgee no longer has the right to retain the pledge, because the pledgee has collected his right, so the basis of retention ceases. 3. The pledgor pays the full debt, and then by chance the pledge perishes in the possession of the pledgee before surrender; then the pledgor will take back what he paid, because due to this destruction the pledgee becomes a collector of his debt, resulting in double collection; therefore, it is necessary to return it to avoid that.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the pledgee's right of retention (habs) over the pledge until the debt is fully paid. It begins by quoting Al-Quduri: the pledgee is not obliged to allow the pledgor to sell the pledge until the debt is paid, because the nature of a pledge is perpetual retention as security. The commentary expands that the pledgee may keep the pledge until payment. Then it addresses three issues explicitly. First: Even if the pledgor pays part of the debt, the pledgee may retain the entire pledge until the remainder is paid, analogized to the seller's right to retain the sold item until full payment (qiyas jaliy). Second: Upon full payment, the pledgee must surrender the pledge because the obstacle (the debt) is removed. Third: If the pledge perishes after full payment but before actual surrender, the pledgor may recover the money paid because the destruction itself satisfies the debt (the pledgee is deemed to have collected via the prior possession), so collecting both the payment and the value of the pledge would be double recovery. This ensures justice.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): The right of retention; the pledgee's entitlement to keep the pledge in his possession as security.
مبیع (mabi'): Sold item; used here as the basis for analogy in retention.
استیفاء (istifa'): Collection or satisfaction of a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pledgor pays half of the debt, what is the pledgee's right regarding the pledge?
A) The pledgee must release half of the pledge.
B) The pledgee may retain the entire pledge until the full debt is paid.
C) The pledgee loses his right to retain the pledge.
D) The pledgor may force the sale of the pledge.

Key Takeaway
A pledgee may retain the entire pledge until the full debt is paid; partial payment does not trigger proportionate release, and destruction after full payment returns the payment to avoid double recovery.

Rescission of Pledge and Right of Retention
Ruling with proof on the effect of rescission on pledge retention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the rescission of a pledge, explain the condition for complete release, and apply the rule to cases of partial payment and destruction.

Core Idea
Rescission does not release the pledge until the debt is paid or the pledge is physically returned.

When two parties rescind a pledge contract, one might think the pledgee must immediately return the pledged item. However, Hanafi law holds that the pledgee retains the item as security until the debt is fully satisfied or the pledgor formally releases the debt. This lesson explores this ruling, its rationale, and its practical consequences, including what happens if the pledge perishes after rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act under discussion is the rescission (faskh) of a pledge (rahn) by mutual agreement.
2
State the ruling on retention
Note that even after rescission, the pledgee retains possession until the debt is received or the pledgor releases the debt. Rescission alone does not end the security interest.
3
Determine when the pledge is truly invalidated
The pledge only becomes invalid (batil) when the pledgee physically returns it to the pledgor for the purpose of rescission. Mere agreement is insufficient.
4
Understand the rationale
The pledge remains guaranteed (mamun) as long as possession and the debt remain. This is why the pledgee’s right of retention persists.
5
Apply the consequence of destruction
If the pledge perishes in the pledgee’s hand after rescission but before return, the debt is considered satisfied if the pledge’s value covers the debt, because the pledge effectively fulfilled its purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك لـو تـفـاسخا الرهن له حبسه ما لم يقبض الدين اويبرئه ولا يبطل الرهن الا بالرد على الراهن على وجه الفسخ لانه يبقى مضمونا ما بقى القبض والدين ولو هلک فی یده سقط الدين اذا كان به وفاء بالدين
لبقاء الرهن
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر دونوں نے رہن کو سح کیا تو مرتہن رہن کو روکے گا جب تک کہ وہ قرض پر قبضہ نہ کرے یا را اہن کو قرض سے بری کر دے اور رہن بالکل نہیں ہوتا مگر راہن کے اوپر فتح سے طریقہ پر واپس کرنے کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ رہن مضمون باقی رہے گا جب تک کہ قبضہ اور دین باقی ہو اور اگر مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض ساقط ہو جائیگا جبکہ اس سے وفاء دین ہو رہن کے باقی
And similarly, if they rescind the pledge, the pledgee retains it until he receives the debt or he [the pledgor] releases him from the debt. And the pledge does not become invalid except by returning it to the pledgor in the manner of rescission, because it remains held as a trust (or guarantee) as long as possession and the debt remain. And if the pledge perishes in his hand, the debt falls if its value suffices for the debt, due to the remaining of the pledge.
Translation: Similarly, if both rescind the pledge, the pledgee will retain the pledge until he takes possession of the debt or the pledgor releases him from the debt. And the pledge is not invalidated except by returning it to the pledgor by way of rescission, because it remains guaranteed as long as possession and the debt remain. And if the pledge perishes in his hand, the debt is dropped if it suffices for the debt, due to the remaining of the pledge.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the rescission (faskh) of the pledge contract. It states that even if both parties rescind the pledge, the pledgee continues to retain the pledge until either: (1) the debt is paid to him, or (2) the pledgor formally releases him from the debt. The pledge is not effectively annulled until the pledgee physically returns it to the pledgor in order to effect the rescission. The reason is that as long as the pledgee remains in possession and the debt remains outstanding, the pledge continues to be held as security (mamun/guaranteed). Further, if the pledge perishes while in the pledgee's possession after rescission but before return, the debt is considered satisfied if the pledge's value covers the debt, because the pledge effectively fulfilled its purpose.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of the pledge contract by mutual agreement.
مضمون (mamun): Held as a trust/guarantee; the pledge remains as a security item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the rescission (faskh) of a pledge become effective?
A) Immediately upon mutual agreement.
B) When the pledgee receives the debt or is released from it, and returns the pledge.
C) Only after a court order.
D) When the pledgee gives permission to the pledgor to sell.

Key Takeaway
Rescission of a pledge does not end the pledgee's right of retention; the pledge remains security until the debt is paid or the pledge is physically returned.

Retention of Pledge After Partial Payment
Ruling with proof via qiyas jaliy from sale to pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the mortgagee's right to retain the entire pledge after partial payment, the obligation to return it after full payment, and the return of payment if the pledge perishes after full payment, and explain the qiyas (analogy) with the seller's right of retention in a sale contract.

Core Idea
The mortgagee may keep the whole pledge until fully paid – analogy to the seller's retention of the sold item.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses three interconnected rulings in the contract of pledge (rahn). It affirms the mortgagee's (murtahin) right to retain the entire pledged property even after partial payment of the debt, drawing a clear qiyas (analogy) with the seller's right in a sale contract. Then it addresses the obligation to return the pledge once the debt is fully paid, and the equitable remedy if the pledge perishes after full payment but before delivery, protecting the pledgor from double recovery. The reasoning is rooted in Hanafi usul using qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage gives rulings for three scenarios: after partial payment, after full payment, and after full payment but before return. Identify each.
These are: (1) mortgagee may keep entire pledge until full payment even after partial payment; (2) after full payment, must return pledge; (3) if pledge perishes after full payment but before return, mortgagee must return the payment received.
2
Trace the qiyas (analogy) to sale
The text explicitly says 'by analogy with the detention of the sold item (ḥabs al-mabīʿ)'. Identify the asl (original case: seller's right to retain sold item until full payment of price), the farʿ (new case: mortgagee's right to retain pledge), and the illah (effective cause: securing full payment of a monetary obligation).
The illah is jaliyyah (clear) – both contracts involve a right to detain property until full payment.
3
Apply the analogy to each scenario
In sale, the seller may keep the entire item until full payment even if part payment is made. Similarly, the mortgagee keeps the entire pledge. After full payment, the basis for retention is gone, so delivery is required. The destruction case is derived from the same principle: after full payment, possession is no longer for security, so the mortgagee cannot benefit from destruction.
The ruling on destruction after full payment protects the pledgor from double recovery.
4
Identify the epistemic weight
This is a ruling from the ẓāhir al-riwāyah (the six core books of Imam Muḥammad) and is muftā bihi. The qiyas used is qiyās jaliy (clear analogy), which is a strong proof in Hanafi uṣūl.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf is noted; the ruling is established.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
Some schools (e.g. Shāfiʿī) may differ on retention after partial payment, possibly requiring proportional release. The Hanafi reliance on qiyas with sale is distinctive.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilāf rooted in different methodologies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قضاه البعض فله ان يحبس كل الرهن حتى يستوفي البقية اعتبارا بحبس المبيع فاذا قضاه الدين قيل له سلم الرهن اليه لانه زال المانع من التسليم لوصول الحق الى مستحقه فلو هلک قبل التسلیم استرد الراهن ما قضاه لانه صار مستوفيا عند الهلاك بالقبض السابق فكان الثانى استيفاء بعد استيفاء فيجب رده.
ترجمہ: اور اگر مرتین کو کچھ قرض ادا کر دیا تو مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ وہ پورا رہن روک نے یہاں تک کہ باقی کو وصول کرے جبس مبیع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے پس جب راہن نے مرتہن کو پورا قرض اداء کر دیا تو مرتہن سے کہا جائیگا کہ رہن راہن کے حوالہ کر اس لئے کہ جو چیز سپرد کرنے سے مانع تھی وہ زائل ہو گئی حق کے اس کے متحقق تک پہنچ جانے کی وجہ سے پس اگر رہن ہلاک ہو گیا سپر د کرنے سے پہلے تو راہن وہ مال واپس لیگا جو مرتہن کو ادا کیا تھا اس لئے کہ مرتہن ہلاکت کے وقت سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے وصول کرنے والا ہو گیا تو دوسرا وصول کرنا وصول کرنے کے بعد وصول کرتا ہوگا پس اس کا ( ثانی کا ) واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا۔
تشریح: اس عبارت میں تین مسائل ہیں۔ ا۔ باب بیچ میں بائع کو حق ہوتا ہے کہ جب تک مشتری شمن ادا نہ کرے صبیع حوالہ نہ کرے بلکہ اپنے پاس روکے رکھے اور اگر مشتری نے کچھ مشن ادا کر دیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تب بھی بائع کو حق ہے کہ پوراشن وصول کرنے تک مبیع کو روکے رکھے اسی طرح اگر راہن نے کچھ قرض ادا کر دیا اور کچھ باقی ہے تو مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ جب تک راہن پورا قرض ادا نہ کرے مرہون کورو کے رکھے۔ ۲۔ جب راہن نے پورا قرض ادا کر دیا تو اب مرتہن کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ مرہون کو اپنے پاس روکے رکھے کیونکہ مرتہن نے اپنا حق وصول کر لیا تو جس بنیاد پر مرتہن کو جس کا حکم تھا وہ بنیاد ختم ہوگئی۔ ۳۔ راہن نے پورا قرض ادا کر دیا اور اداء دین کے بعد اتفاق سے مرتہن کے پاس مرہون ہلاک ہو گیا تو راہن نے جو قرض ادا کیا تھا اس کو واپس لے گا کیونکہ مرتہن اس ہلاکت کی وجہ سے اپنا قرض وصول کرنے والا ہو گیا تو یہ ڈبل وصول ہو جائے گا اس سے بچنے کے لئے اس کی واپسی ضروری ہے۔
And if he pays some of it, he has the right to detain the entire pledge until he recovers the remainder, by analogy with the detention of the sold item. So when he pays the debt, it is said to him: 'Deliver the pledge to him' because the impediment to delivery has been removed due to the right reaching its claimant. So if it perishes before delivery, the pledgor recovers what he paid because at the time of destruction he becomes a recoverer by virtue of the prior possession, so the second is a recovery after recovery, so its return is obligatory. Translation: And if the mortgagee pays some of the debt, the mortgagee has the right to detain the entire pledge until he collects the remainder, by analogy with the detention of the sold item. Then when the pledgor pays the full debt, it is said to the mortgagee: 'Hand over the pledge to the pledgor' because the barrier to delivery has been removed due to the right reaching its claimant. So if the pledge perishes before delivery, the pledgor takes back the wealth he paid to the mortgagee, because at the time of destruction, the mortgagee becomes a recoverer of his debt by virtue of his prior possession, so the second recovery is a recovery after recovery, so its return is obligatory. Explanation: In this phrase there are three issues. 1. In the chapter of sale, the seller has the right not to hand over the sold item until the buyer pays the price, and if the buyer pays part and part remains, the seller still has the right to detain the entire sold item until full payment. Similarly, if the pledgor pays part of the debt and part remains, the mortgagee has the right to detain the entire pledge until the pledgor pays the entire debt. 2. When the pledgor pays the entire debt, the mortgagee no longer has the right to detain the pledge, because the mortgagee has received his right and the basis for detention is gone. 3. The pledgor pays the full debt and then accidentally the pledge perishes in the mortgagee's hand. Then the pledgor will take back the debt he paid, because the mortgagee, by this destruction, becomes a recoverer of his debt, so this would be double recovery; to avoid this, its return is necessary.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school, applying qiyas (analogy) to the rules of sale. It addresses three linked issues in the contract of rahn. First, just as a seller in a sale contract may retain the entire sold item until full payment of the price, so too a mortgagee (murtahin) may retain the entire pledged property (marhun) until full payment of the debt, even if part of the debt has been paid. This is based on the principle of حبس المبيع (retention of the sold item). Second, once the debt is fully paid, the impediment to delivery is removed, and the mortgagee must return the pledge to the pledgor (rahin). Third, if after full payment but before physical return the pledge is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, the mortgagee is deemed to have recovered the debt by virtue of his prior possession at the time of destruction, so he must return the payment received, otherwise he would recover twice. This protects the pledgor from injustice. The text uses the term اعتبارا بحبس المبيع, explicitly showing the qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) between sale and pledge.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where property is placed as security for a debt; the pledged property is called marhun.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge as security for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The debtor who gives property as pledge.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession; in rahn, valid possession is essential for the contract to be binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledgor pays half the debt, what is the mortgagee's right regarding the pledged property?
A) He must release half the pledge proportionally.
B) He may retain the entire pledge until full payment.
C) He must release the entire pledge and sue for the remaining debt.
D) He may sell the pledge to recover the debt.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee may retain the entire pledged property until the debt is fully paid, even after partial payment, and if the pledge perishes after full payment but before delivery, the payment must be returned to avoid double recovery.

Effect of Mutual Rescission on Pledge: Continued Detention and Consequences of Destruction
Ruling on status of pledge after mutual rescission and effect of destruction before return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a mutual rescission (faskh) of a pledge does not invalidate the pledge until the pledged property is actually returned, and apply this rule to determine the status of the pledge in scenarios involving verbal rescission and subsequent destruction.

Core Idea
A pledge is not invalidated by mere words; only actual return ends the mortgagee's right of detention and the property's security status.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a common practical question: if both pledgor and mortgagee verbally agree to cancel the pledge but the property remains with the mortgagee, is the pledge still valid? The Hanafi answer is clear – the pledge endures until physical redelivery. We will examine the reasoning (ta'lil) and the consequences if the property is destroyed in the interim, and compare with possible views of other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sub-rulings
The passage covers: (1) continued right of detention after verbal rescission, (2) invalidation requires actual return, (3) destruction after verbal rescission but before return discharges the debt if the pledge's value covers it.
These are cumulative: they share the same underlying rationale.
2
Understand the underlying rationale (ta'lil)
The reasoning: 'because it remains a security as long as possession and debt remain.' The pledge's legal effect (madhmun) persists as long as both elements are present. Verbal rescission alone does not sever the connection.
This is the core legal principle driving all three rulings.
3
Apply the ta'lil to the destruction scenario
Since the pledge continues in effect, destruction in the mortgagee's hand is treated like any other destruction during a valid pledge. If the value equals the debt, the debt is discharged; if less, the balance remains due from the pledgor.
The mortgagee's possession is still through the pledge contract, not as a mere custodian.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
Other schools may hold that verbal rescission suffices to invalidate. The Hanafi insistence on actual return is distinctive and protects the mortgagee's interest until physical redelivery.
This difference stems from different conceptions of the nature of rahn as a contract.
5
Draw practical conclusions
A mortgagee who verbally agrees to cancel but does not return the property retains the right to detain and the property remains at risk; destruction discharges the debt automatically if value suffices.
The ruling provides legal certainty and prevents exploitation.

Source Text

وكذلك لو تفاسخا الرهن له حبسه ما لم يقبض الدين او يبرئه ولا يبطل الرهن الا بالرد على الراهن على وجه الفسخ لانه يبقى مضمونا ما بقى القبض والدين ولو هلک فی یده سقط الدين اذا كان به وفاء بالدين لبقاء الرهن.
ترجمہ: اور ایسے ہی اگر دونوں نے رہن کو سح کیا تو مرتہن رہن کو روکے گا جب تک کہ وہ قرض پر قبضہ نہ کرے یا را اہن کو قرض سے بری کر دے اور رہن بالکل نہیں ہوتا مگر راہن کے اوپر فتح سے طریقہ پر واپس کرنے کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ رہن مضمون باقی رہے گا جب تک کہ قبضہ اور دین باقی ہو اور اگر مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض ساقط ہو جائیگا جبکہ اس سے وفاء دین ہو رہن کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح: اس عبادت میں بھی تین مسائل ہیں۔ ۱ - جیسے مرتہن کو حق ہے کہ جب تک اپنا قرض وصول نہ کرے تب تک مرہون کو روکے رکھے اسی طرح اگر راہن و مرتہن دونو انسے رہن کو زبانی فسخ کر لیا، مگر ہنوز مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہے تو ابھی رہن فسخ نہ ہو گا لہذا مرتین کو برابر اس کے روکنے کا حق ہو گا جب تک کہ راہن اس کا قرض نہ ادا کر دے یا مرتهن راہن کو قرض سے بری کر دے بری کرنے کے بعد اور قرض کو ادا کرنے کے بعد مرتہن کو روکنے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ ۲ - رہن اس وقت باطل ہو گا جب کہ صبح کے طریقے پر مرتین رہن راہن کو سپرد کر دے ورنہ جب تک دین کے ساتھ قبضہ مرتهن باقی رہے گا اس پر رہن کے احکام جاری ہوں گے اور حسب سابق رہن مضمون ہوگا۔ ۳ - رہن کا بطلان زبانی مسیح سے جب ہوگا جب کہ مرہون راہن کے سپرد کر دیا جائے ورنہ نہیں ہو گا لہذا اگر زبانی مسیح کے بعد مرہون واپس نہیں کیا گیا اور مرتہن کے قبضہ میں وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو یہ رہن مضمون ہوگا اور اگر اس کی قیمت قرض کے بقدر ہے تو قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اگر کم ہے تو حسب حکم سابق مابقی کو راہن سے وصول کرے گا اور یہاں قرض ساقط ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ واپس کرنے سے پہلے پہلے رہن باقی ہے لہذا اس پر رہن کے احکام جاری ہوں گے۔
And likewise if they mutually rescind the pledge, he has the right to detain it as long as he has not received the debt or acquitted him. And the pledge is not invalidated except by returning it to the pledgor in the manner of rescission, because it remains a security as long as possession and debt remain. And if it perishes in his hand, the debt falls if its value covers the debt, due to the continued existence of the pledge. Translation: And similarly if both rescind the pledge, the mortgagee will detain it until he receives possession of the debt or acquits the pledgor. And the pledge is not invalidated except by returning it to the pledgor in the manner of rescission, because the pledge remains a security as long as possession and debt remain. And if the pledged property perishes in the mortgagee's possession, the debt falls if its value covers the debt, due to the continued existence of the pledge. Explanation: In this phrase there are three issues. 1. Just as the mortgagee has the right to detain the pledge until he receives his debt, similarly if the pledgor and mortgagee both verbally rescind the pledge but the pledged property is still in the mortgagee's possession, the pledge is not invalidated yet; thus the mortgagee still has the right to detain it until the pledgor pays the debt or the mortgagee acquits the pledgor. After acquittal or payment, the mortgagee has no right to detain. 2. The pledge is invalidated only when the mortgagee returns it to the pledgor in the manner of rescission; otherwise, as long as possession and debt remain, the rulings of pledge continue, and it remains a security. 3. Invalidation of the pledge by verbal rescission occurs only when the pledge is actually returned; if it is not returned and perishes in the mortgagee's hand, it remains a security: if its value equals the debt, the debt falls; if less, the balance is collected from the pledgor as before. The reason the debt falls is that the pledge remains before return, so its rulings continue.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of mutual rescission (faskh) on a pledge contract. It addresses three related issues. First, if both parties verbally agree to cancel the pledge but the property remains in the mortgagee's possession, the pledge is not actually invalidated; the mortgagee retains the right of detention until the debt is paid or the mortgagee formally acquits the pledgor. Second, the pledge is only invalidated 'by return to the pledgor in the manner of rescission' (بالرد على الراهن على وجه الفسخ) – actual physical return is required. Third, if after verbal rescission but before return the pledge is destroyed, the mortgagee's possession still operates as a security: if the value of the pledge equals the debt, the debt is discharged (sutqut al-dayn); if less, the remaining balance is due from the pledgor. This is because the pledge remains 'madhmun' (liable/secured) as long as possession and debt remain. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on the survival of the pledge contract's effects until actual redelivery.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Mutual rescission or cancellation of a contract by the parties.
مضمون (madhmun): Liable or under security; the pledged property remains a guarantee for the debt as long as it is in the mortgagee's possession.
وفاء (wafa'): Sufficiency; when the value of the pledged property is enough to cover the debt, destruction leads to discharge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The debt is discharged completely.
C) The mortgagee must pay the value to the pledgor.
D) The pledgor gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
A pledge remains valid and its security effects continue until the pledged property is physically returned to the pledgor, even after verbal rescission.

Mortgagee Cannot Benefit from Pledge Without Permission
Ruling prohibiting mortgagee from using pledge, with riba warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mortgagee benefiting from pledged property and explain why even with permission it may be considered riba.

Core Idea
A mortgagee's right is detention only, not use; any benefit without return is riba.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical principle in Islamic finance: the mortgagee cannot use the pledged asset for personal gain. While an exception is made for the owner's permission, a later warning clarifies that such benefit is still prohibited as riba. Understanding this helps prevent usurious practices disguised as loans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the mortgagee is prohibited from doing: deriving any benefit (intifa') from the pledged property, such as using a slave for service, dwelling in a house, or wearing a garment.
The ruling is prohibition (haram).
2
State the proof (dalil)
The mortgagee's right is limited to detention (habs) only, not enjoyment (intifa'). This is the foundational principle derived from the nature of the contract.
The proof is a legal maxim, not an explicit text.
3
Note the exception and the warning
The text initially permits benefit if the owner (pledgor) gives permission. However, a warning (tanbih) immediately follows, stating that any benefit on a loan is riba, even with permission, because riba does not become lawful by consent.
This creates a tension: the exception seems overridden by the riba prohibition.
4
Analyze the role of custom
The passage invokes the maxim 'al-maruf ka al-mashrut' (custom is like a condition). If benefiting from pledges is customary, it may be considered as if stipulated, but the riba prohibition remains paramount.
The author of Al-Hidayah's ruling may be contextual to a time when such benefit was not customary.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a mortgagee benefits without permission, the contract is unaffected but the mortgagee is sinful and must compensate for any loss? The warning makes it a riba issue, potentially invalidating the loan if benefit is received.
This differs from other schools that allow benefit with permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للمرتهن ان ينتفع بالرهن لا باستخدام ولا سكنى ولا لبس الا ان ياذن له المالك لان له حق الحبس دون الانتفاع.
ترجمہ: اور مرتن کوحق نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہون سے نفع اٹھائے نہ خدمت لینے کے طریقہ پراور نہ کئی کے طریقہ اورنہ پہنے کے طریقہ پر مگر یہ کہ اس کو مالک اجازت دیدے اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو روکنے کا حق ہے نہ کہ انتفاع کا۔
تشریح: مرتہن کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہون سے نفع اٹھائے یعنی اگر وہ غلام ہے تو اس سے خدمت لینے کا جواز نہیں ہے اور اگر گھر ہے تو اس میں رہنے کا جواز نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ کپڑا ہے تو اس کو پہنے کا جواز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مرتہن کو انتفاع کا حق نہیں بلکہ صرف جس کا حکم ہوتا ہے ہاں اگر راہن اجازت دیدے تو پھر انتفاع جائز ہے۔
تنبیه: مرہون سے انتفاع حرام ہے اور سود ہے اگر چہ را بہن بھی اجازت دیدے اس لئے کہ سود اجازت دینے سے حلال نہیں ہو جاتا اور المعروف کا لمشروط قاعدہ کلیہ ہے اور اب غالب یہی ہے کہ لوگ دوسروں کی زمین رہن پر اس لئے لیتے ہیں کہ اس سے آمدنی حاصل کریں تو صاحب ہدایہ کا فرمان ان کے زمانہ پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ ان کے زمانہ میں انتفاع بالمرہون کا رواج نہیں تھا دیکھئے شافی ص ۳۱۰ ج ۵ ۔
And the mortgagee does not have the right to benefit from the pledge, not by using as a servant, nor by dwelling, nor by wearing, unless the owner permits him, because he has the right of detention, not the right of enjoyment. Translation: And the mortgagee does not have the right to benefit from the pledge, not by way of taking service (if a slave), nor by way of dwelling (if a house), nor by way of wearing (if a garment), unless the owner allows. Because the mortgagee has the right to detain, not to benefit. Explanation: It is not permissible for the mortgagee to benefit from the pledge: if it is a slave, he cannot take service; if a house, he cannot live in it; if a garment, he cannot wear it. Because the mortgagee does not have the right to benefit, but only the right to detain. However, if the pledgor permits, then benefiting is permissible. Warning: Benefiting from the pledge is prohibited and is riba (usury), even if the pledgor permits it, because riba does not become lawful by permission. And the legal maxim is 'the custom is like a condition.' But nowadays, people take others' land on pledge to earn income; the author of al-Hidayah's statement may be applicable to his time when such use was not customary. See Shafi p. 310 vol. 5.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school stating that the mortgagee (murtahin) is prohibited from deriving any personal benefit from the pledged property (marhun). The text explicitly lists three examples: using a slave for service (istikdam), dwelling in a house (sukna), and wearing a garment (lubs). The proof is clear: 'he has the right of detention, not the right of enjoyment' (له حق الحبس دون الانتفاع). This is a fundamental principle in rahn: the mortgagee's right is limited to security, not ownership. An exception is given: if the owner (pledgor) permits, then benefit is allowed. However, a important warning (tanbih) follows: benefiting from the pledge is actually riba (usury) and thus haram, even with the pledgor's permission. This is because any loan that brings benefit to the lender is usury. The author of al-Hidayah notes that this ruling may be contextual to his time when such benefit was not customary; but the general principle remains that unauthorized benefit is riba. The text also references the legal maxim 'al-maruf ka al-mashrut' (the customary practice is like a stipulated condition), implying that if custom allows benefit, it may be considered as if it were stipulated, but still the basic prohibition of riba applies.

Key Terms
انتفاع (intifa'): Deriving benefit or use from the pledged property, such as service, dwelling, or wearing.
سود (sūd): Usury/riba; any extra benefit obtained from a loan is riba.
المعروف كالمشروط (al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut): A legal maxim meaning 'the customary practice is like a stipulated condition.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mortgagee cannot use the pledge; owner's permission does not legitimize what is riba.

Three Issues Regarding the Voiding of a Pawn
Explains three conditions for voiding a pawn contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that void a pawn contract and apply the rule that mere verbal rescission does not void without physical return.

Core Idea
Verbal rescission alone does not void a pawn; only physical return or debt discharge ends the contract.

The pawn contract is a security arrangement that continues until the debt is satisfied or the pawn is physically returned. This passage expands on three critical rulings that clarify when a pawn is considered void and how liability is affected. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the contract's effects in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three issues
Read the passage to identify each of the three distinct rulings (masa'il) about voiding the pawn.
The first issue concerns verbal rescission without return; the second states that voiding requires physical return; the third addresses liability if the pawn is destroyed after verbal rescission but before return.
2
Extract the condition for voiding in each issue
For each issue, determine what action or event makes the pawn void. The first issue: voiding does not occur by mere verbal agreement. The second: only physical return voids. The third: voiding requires return, otherwise the pawn remains in effect.
The condition for voiding is consistently the physical return of the pawn (or satisfaction of the debt, as implied in the first issue).
3
Analyze the role of possession (qabd)
Possession by the mortgagee is central. As long as possession continues, the pawn's rulings apply, including detention right and liability.
Hanafi fiqh considers qabd essential for the validity of the pawn contract.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a case where both parties verbally cancel the pawn but the pawn stays with the mortgagee. Determine the status and liability if the pawn is destroyed.
Apply the principle: pawn remains valid; mortgagee is liable (damin) for the value.
5
Summarize the legal effects
After understanding the three issues, state the overall rule: The pawn is only voided by physical return or when the debt is paid or released. Verbal rescission alone leaves the contract intact.

Explanation: In this chapter also there are three issues. Similarly, the mortgagee has the right to detain the pawn until he recovers his debt. Similarly, if the pledgor and mortgagee both verbally rescind the pawn, but the pawn is still in the mortgagee's possession, then the pawn is not yet rescinded. Therefore, the mortgagee still has the right to detain it until the pledgor pays the debt or the mortgagee releases the pledgor from the debt. After release or payment, the mortgagee has no right to detain. 2. The pawn is voided only when the mortgagee surrenders the pawn to the pledgor in the morning manner. The reason the debt is discharged here is that before return, the pawn remains intact, so its rulings continue.

Commentary
This passage presents three interconnected rulings about the voiding (batalan) of a pawn contract (rahn). The commentary expands on the base text, clarifying that mere verbal rescission without physical return of the pawn does not invalidate the contract. The mortgagee's right of detention (haqq al-habs) persists until the debt is paid or released. The first issue emphasizes that the mortgagee retains detention rights even after verbal rescission. The second issue states that the pawn is voided only when the mortgagee returns possession to the pledgor. The third issue clarifies that if the pawn is destroyed after verbal rescission but before return, the mortgagee remains liable (damin) and the debt is discharged up to the pawn's value. The key principle is that possession (qabd) is integral to the pawn contract, and its effects continue until possession is actually surrendered.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): pawn/pledge: a contract where property is given as security for a debt.
بطلان (būṭlān): nullification/voiding of the contract.
مضمون (madhmūn): guaranteed/liable; the pawn is held as a guarantee subject to liability rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both pledgor and mortgagee verbally agree to cancel the pawn, but the mortgagee keeps possession, and the pawn is later destroyed, what is the ruling?
A) The pawn is void and the mortgagee is not liable.
B) The pawn remains valid and the mortgagee must compensate the pledgor.
C) The pawn is void but the mortgagee must return the pawn's value.
D) The debt is automatically discharged.

Key Takeaway
A pawn contract is not voided by verbal agreement alone; physical return of the pawn is required, and the mortgagee remains liable until such return.

The Prohibition of Mortgagee Benefiting from the Pawn
States the prohibition against mortgagee benefiting from pawned item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mortgagee benefiting from a pawn and explain why it constitutes riba even with the pledgor's permission.

Core Idea
Benefiting from a pawn is haram because any gain on a loan is riba — even with permission.

In a mortgage (rahn), the mortgagee holds the pawn as security for a debt. A common question is whether the mortgagee may use the pawned item. This lesson examines the clear Hanafi ruling: benefiting from the pawn is prohibited, and even the pledgor's permission does not make it lawful because it is considered riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the mortgagee has no right to benefit from the pawn. Determine the legal category of this prohibition.
The hukm is haram, not merely makruh.
2
Examine the scope of prohibition
The text lists examples: service, dwelling, wearing. Generalize: any form of benefit (intifa') from the pawn is included.
The prohibition covers all usufruct.
3
Analyze the effect of pledgor's permission
The passage initially says benefiting is allowed with permission, but the caution (tanbih) clarifies that even with permission it remains haram as riba.
This is the key point: permission does not nullify the prohibition of riba.
4
Apply the maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut'
The commentator notes that this maxim (custom is like a condition) is general but does not override explicit prohibitions like riba.
Custom cannot legalize what is inherently haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للمرتهن ان ينتفع بالرهن لا باستخدام ولا سكنى ولا لبس الا ان ياذن له المالك لان له حق الحبس دون الانتفاع
ترجمہ اور مرتن کوحق نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہون سے نفع اٹھائے نہ خدمت لینے کے طریقہ پراور نہ کئی کے طریقہ اورنہ پہنے کے طریقہ پر مگر یہ کہ اس کو مالک اجازت دیدے اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو روکنے کا حق ہے نہ کہ انتفاع کا۔ تشریح مرتہن کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہون سے نفع اٹھائے یعنی اگر وہ غلام ہے تو اس سے خدمت لینے کا جواز نہیں ہے اور اگر گھر ہے تو اس میں رہنے کا جواز نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ کپڑا ہے تو اس کو پہنے کا جواز نہیں ہے کیونکہ مرتہن کو انتفاع کا حق نہیں بلکہ صرف جس کا حکم ہوتا ہے ہاں اگر راہن اجازت دیدے تو پھر انتفاع جائز ہے۔
تنبیه مرہون سے انتفاع حرام ہے اور سود ہے اگر چہ را بہن بھی اجازت دیدے اس لئے کہ سود اجازت دینے سے حلال نہیں ہو جاتا اور المعروف کا لمشروط قاعدہ کلیہ ہے اور اب غالب یہی ہے کہ لوگ دوسروں کی زمین رہن پر اس لئے لیتے ہیں کہ اس سے آمدنی حاصل کریں تو صاحب ہدایہ کا فرمان ان کے زمانہ پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ ان کے زمانہ میں انتفاع بالمرہون کا رواج نہیں تھا دیکھئے شافی ص ۳۱۰ ج ۵۔
And the mortgagee has no right to benefit from the pawn, neither by using its service, nor by dwelling, nor by wearing, unless the owner (pledgor) gives permission, because he has the right of detention, not the right of benefit. Translation: And the mortgagee does not have the right to benefit from the pawn, neither by way of taking service, nor by way of dwelling, nor by way of wearing, unless the owner permits, because the mortgagee has the right to detain, not to benefit. Explanation: It is not permissible for the mortgagee to benefit from the pawn. That is, if it is a slave, taking service is not permissible; if it is a house, dwelling in it is not permissible; if it is a garment, wearing it is not permissible, because the mortgagee has no right to benefit, only the right to detain. Yes, if the pledgor gives permission, then benefiting is permissible. Caution: Benefiting from the pawn is haram and is riba (usury), even if the pledgor gives permission, because riba does not become halal by permission. And the principle 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut' (custom is like stipulation) is a general maxim. Nowadays, people take others' land as pawn with the intention of earning income from it, so the author of Hidayah's statement can be interpreted as pertaining to his own time, when benefiting from pawn was not common. See Shafi vol.5 p.310.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental ruling: the mortgagee (murtahin) has no right to derive any benefit (intifa') from the pawned item (marhun). The text lists three examples: service from a slave, dwelling in a house, wearing a garment. The mortgagee's right is solely detention (habs) to secure the debt, not usage. The commentary adds a crucial caution (tanbih): even if the pledgor (rahin) explicitly permits the mortgagee to use the item, it remains haram and constitutes riba (usury) because the benefit derived from a pawn is considered a prohibited increase on the debt. The famous maxim 'al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut' (what is customary is like a stipulated condition) does not override the prohibition of riba. The commentator notes that the author of al-Hidayah's ruling might have been specific to his era when such practice was uncommon; today, taking land as pawn for income is widespread and remains prohibited.

Key Terms
انتفاع (intifā'): deriving benefit or utility from the pawned item.
ربا (ribā): usury/unlawful increase; benefiting from a pawn is considered a form of riba.
المعروف كالمشروط (al-ma'rūf ka al-mashrūṭ): customary practice has the force of a stipulated condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Benefiting from a pawn is haram and constitutes riba; permission from the pledgor does not make it halal.

The Mortgagee May Not Sell or Lease the Pawn
Prohibits the mortgagee from selling or leasing the pawn without the pledgor's authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the mortgagee's sale/lease of the pawn and explain why the pawn contract remains valid despite the transgression.

Core Idea
The mortgagee has no right to sell or lease the pawn because he lacks authority over benefit; transgression does not invalidate the contract.

The mortgagee's right over the pawn is limited to detention. This lesson explains that he cannot transfer benefit to others, as he himself lacks the legal capacity. However, if he does so, the pawn contract remains intact, and he is merely a transgressor liable for damages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited actions
The passage explicitly prohibits the mortgagee from selling, leasing (ijara), or lending (ariya) the pawn without the pledgor's authorization.
These are all acts of transferring benefit or ownership.
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
The prohibition is based on the mortgagee's lack of legal authority (wilaya) to benefit from the pawn himself. Since he cannot benefit, he cannot delegate that benefit to others.
This reasoning is a form of qiyas: the mortgagee's position is analogous to someone without ownership or agency.
3
Determine the consequence of transgression
If the mortgagee nonetheless sells, leases, or lends, he commits ta'addi (transgression). However, this does not nullify the original pawn contract; it remains valid.
The transgression is a separate act that creates liability but does not affect the contract's validity per Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the exception
The mortgagee may sell the pawn if explicitly authorized by the pledgor. The passage only mentions authorization for sale, not for lease or loan.
Scholars extend this to any act requiring permission; the exception is specific to the pledgor's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس له ان يبيع الابتسليط من الراهن وليس له ان يواجر و يعير لانه ليس له ولاية الانتفاع بنفسه فلا یملک تسليط غيره عليه فان فعل كان متعد يا ولا يبطل عقد الرهن بالتعدى
ترجمہ اور مرتہن کو حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ مرہون کو نیچے مگر راہن کی جانب سے مسلط کئے جانے کے ساتھ اور حق نہیں ہے اس کو کہ مرہون کو اجارہ پر دے اور عاریت پر دے اس لئے کہ اس کو خود انتفاع کی ولایت نہیں ہے تو وہ انتفاع پر اپنے غیر کو مسلط کرنے کا مالک نہ ہوگا پس اگر مرتہن نے ایسا کیا تو وہ زیادتی کرنے والا ہے اور اس تعدی کی وجہ سے عقد رہن باطل نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح مرتین مرہون کو فروخت نہیں کر سکتا ہاں اگر راہن اجازت دے تو فروخت کر سکتا ہے اسی طرح مرتہن اس کو اجارہ پر یا اعمارہ پر نہیں دے سکتا کیونکہ جب مرتہن کو خود اس سے نفع اٹھانے کا حق نہیں ہے تو دوسروں کو نفع اٹھوانی کا کیونکر حق ہو سکتا ہے لیکن اگر مرتہن نے اس کو اجارہ وغیرہ پر دیدیا تو یہ اس کی زیادتی ہے مگر اس زیادتی کی وجہ سے عقد رہن باطل نہ ہوگا بلکہ عقدر من برقرار ہے۔
And he (the mortgagee) does not have the right to sell it except by being authorized by the pledgor. And he does not have the right to lease it or lend it, because he has no authority (wilaya) to benefit from it himself, so he cannot authorize others to benefit. If he does so, he is a transgressor (mut'addi), and the pawn contract is not nullified by the transgression. Translation: And the mortgagee does not have the right to sell the pawn except with authorization from the pledgor. And he does not have the right to lease it or lend it as a loan (ariya), because he himself has no authority of benefit, so he cannot authorize others. If he does so, he is a transgressor, and the pawn contract is not invalidated by this transgression. Explanation: The mortgagee cannot sell the pawn; however, if the pledgor permits, he can sell. Similarly, the mortgagee cannot lease it or give it on loan (ariya), because when he himself has no right to benefit, how can he give others the right to benefit? But if the mortgagee does lease it, it is his transgression, yet the pawn contract remains valid and is not nullified.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous lesson by addressing the mortgagee's authority over the pawn regarding third parties. The mortgagee cannot sell, lease (ijara), or lend (ariya) the pawn to others. The only exception is if the pledgor explicitly authorizes the sale. The underlying reason (ta'lil) is that the mortgagee lacks the legal capacity (wilaya) to benefit from the pawn himself; therefore, he cannot delegate that benefit to others. If he nevertheless does so, he commits transgression (ta'addi), but this transgression does not nullify the original pawn contract. The contract remains intact because the transgression is separate from the contract's validity. The commentary emphasizes that the mortgagee's right is limited to detention, and any transfer of use or ownership without permission is impermissible.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addī): transgression; acting beyond one's legal authority.
ولایت (wilāyah): legal authority or competence to act on behalf of another or over property.
اجارہ (ijārah): lease/rental contract.

Key Takeaway

From Whom the Mortgagee May Safeguard the Pawn
Defines permissible custodians of a pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who may be entrusted with safeguarding a pawn without incurring liability, and identify the criterion for 'household' ('iyal) in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A pawn is a trust; the mortgagee may only entrust it to household members; otherwise he is liable.

The mortgagee is obligated to safeguard the pawn, but he need not do it personally. This lesson clarifies exactly whom he may delegate the task to without becoming liable for loss. The ruling rests on an analogy to a deposit (wadi'ah): the pawn is a trust in his hands, so the same rules apply. Understanding the precise definition of 'household' ('iyal) is critical—not every employee or relative qualifies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is safeguarding the pawn (hifz al-rahn). The ruling is that the mortgagee must safeguard it properly; he may do so personally or through specific individuals.
The default is that the mortgagee is liable if he entrusts it to an unauthorized person.
2
List the permissible custodians
The text lists: himself, his wife, his child, and his servant who resides in his household ('iyal). These are considered extensions of himself for safeguarding.
The child must also be in his household; a child living elsewhere is not included.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The pawn is a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands, analogous to a deposit (wadi'ah). Just as a depositee may entrust the deposit to household members, so may the mortgagee.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) based on the shared 'illa of being a trust.
4
Apply the criterion for 'iyal
The decisive factor is residence in the mortgagee's house, not obligation of maintenance. Wife, children, resident servants, monthly workers are included; daily laborers are not.
A partner in a commenda partnership (mufawada) is also considered like a household member.
5
Determine the consequence of entrusting to an outsider
If the mortgagee entrusts the pawn to someone not in his household, he becomes liable (damin) for its value if it is lost. Whether the outsider also becomes liable is a matter of ikhtilaf, detailed in the book of Wadi'ah.
The mortgagee's liability arises from transgression (ta'addi) in delegating improperly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وللمرتهن أن يحفظ الرهن بنفسه وزوجته وولده وخادمه الذى فى عياله قال رضى الله عنه معده ان يكون الولد فى عياله ايضا وهذا لان عينه امانة في يده فصار كا لوديعة وان حفظه بغير من فى عياله او اودعه ضمن وهل يضمن الثاني فهو على الخلاف وقد بينا جميع ذلك بدلائله في الوديعة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور متن کو جائز ہے کہ وہ رہن کی خود حفاظت کرے اور اپنی بیوی کے ذریعہ اور اپنے لڑکے کے ذریعہ اور اپنے اس خادم کے ذریعہ جو اس کی عیال میں ہے مصنف نے فرمایا اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ وہ بچہ جو اس کی عیال میں ہو اور یہ اس لئے کہ معین رہن مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہے تو یہ ودیعت کے مثل ہو گیا اور اگر اس نے حفاظت اس شخص کے غیر کے ساتھ کی جو اس کی عیال میں ہے یا اس کو ودیعت رکھدیا ہو تو مرتہن ضامن ہو گا اور کیا راہن دوسرے کو ضامن بنائے گا تو یہ اختلاف معروف پر ہے اور ہم ان تمام باتوں کو مع ان کے دلائل کے ودیعت میں بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح مرتہن پر ضروری ہے کہ رہن کی حفاظت یا تو خود کرے یا اپنی بیوی اور اس لڑکے یا خادم سے کرائے جو مرتہن کی عیال میں ہوں ، ورنہ اگر دوسروں کے ذریعہ حفاظت کرائے گا تو مرتہن بصورت ہلاکت مرہون پر صب کے مثل پوری قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ تنبیه - عیال ہونے کا مدار اس کے گھر میں رہنا ہے خواہ اس پر اس کا نفقہ واجب ہو یا نہ ہو جیسے زوجہ اور اس کی اولا د اور اس کا خادم یا اس کا ماہانہ نوکر سب اس کی عیال میں شمار ہونگے جو یومیہ کا مزدور ہے وہ عیال میں داخل نہ ہوگا، نیز شریک شرکت مفاوضہ دعنان بھی عیال کے قائم مقام ہیں نیز زوجہ اور لڑکے کیلئے اس کی عیال میں ہونا شرط نہیں ہے شامی ص ۳۱۳ ج ۵
تنبیه معین رہن ودیعت امانت ہے اور امانت کے یہی احکام ہیں جو مذکور ہوئے۔ تنبیہ مصنف نے اس کی پوری تفصیل ہدایہ ص ۲۵۷ ج ۳ پر بیان کی ہے ایک نظر اس کا مطالعہ کر لیا جائے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And the mortgagee may safeguard the pawn himself, and through his wife, his child, and his servant who is in his household (fi 'iyalihi). The author (of al-Hidayah) said: The meaning is that the child is also in his household. This is because the specific pawn is an amanah (trust) in his hand, so it becomes like a wadi'ah (deposit). If he safeguards it through someone not in his household, or deposits it with someone, then the mortgagee becomes liable (damin). Will the second person (the depositee) also be liable? That is a matter of ikhtilaf (dispute), and we have explained all that with its proofs in the book of Wadi'ah. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And it is permissible for the mortgagee to safeguard the pawn himself, and through his wife, his child, and his servant who is in his household. The author said: The meaning is that the child is also in his household. This is because the specific pawn is a trust in his hand, so it becomes like a deposit. If he safeguards it through someone not in his household, or deposits it, then the mortgagee becomes liable. And will the second party be liable? That is a matter of ikhtilaf, and we have explained all that with its proofs in the book of Wadi'ah. Explanation: It is obligatory for the mortgagee to safeguard the pawn either himself or through his wife, child, or servant who is in his household. Otherwise, if he entrusts safeguarding to others, then upon destruction, the mortgagee is liable for the full price like the price (sab' mithl). Caution: The criterion for being in the household (iyal) is residing in his house, whether or not maintenance (nafaqah) is obligatory. So the wife, children, servant, or monthly worker are all considered household members. A daily wage earner is not included. Also, a partner in a commenda partnership (mufawada) is considered like a household member. The wife and children do not require being in his household as a condition (Shami vol.5 p.313). Caution: The specific pawn is a trust (amanah) and these are the rulings of trust. Caution: The author has detailed this fully in al-Hidayah vol.3 p.257; one should study that.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissible custodians of the pawn when the mortgagee is not personally safeguarding it. The mortgagee may entrust the pawn to his wife, his child, or his servant who are part of his household (iyal). The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the pawn is an amanah (trust) in the mortgagee's hands, analogous to a wadi'ah (deposit). The rules of wadi'ah apply: entrusting to a household member is considered like safeguarding oneself, but entrusting to an outsider makes the mortgagee liable (damin) if the pawn is lost. The commentary clarifies that 'household' includes anyone who resides in the house, regardless of whether maintenance is obligatory. A daily laborer is not considered part of the household. The text also notes a dispute (ikhtilaf) about whether the third-party custodian becomes liable; this is detailed in the book of Wadi'ah and not repeated here. The overall principle is that the mortgagee must exercise the same level of care as for a trust, and deviation results in liability.

Key Terms
عیال ('iyāl): household/dependents who reside with the mortgagee.
ودیعت (wadī'ah): deposit; the pawn is treated like a deposit for safeguarding rules.
ضمان (ḍamān): liability; mortgagee becomes liable for the pawn's value if lost due to improper safeguarding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee may entrust the pawn only to household members; entrusting to outsiders makes him liable.

Mortgagee's Disposal of Pawn Without Permission
Ruling that mortgagee cannot sell, lease, or lend pawn without permission; transgression does not void contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mortgagee's unauthorized sale, lease, or lending of the pawn and explain why the contract remains valid.

Core Idea
Unauthorized use of the pawn by the mortgagee is haram, but it does not void the pawn contract.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the Hidayah regarding the mortgagee's (murtahin) powers over the pawned item. The mortgagee is not allowed to sell, lease, or lend the pawn without the pawner's explicit permission. However, even if he does so, the pawn contract remains valid—only the mortgagee becomes a transgressor and is liable for any loss. This ruling protects the pawner's security while deterring misuse by the mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Acts
The mortgagee cannot sell, lease, or lend the pawn without permission from the pawner.
2
Understand the Rationale (Talil)
The mortgagee has no right to benefit from the pawn himself, so he cannot authorize others to benefit.
The illa is his lack of authority over the usufruct.
3
Recognize the Consequence of Transgression
If the mortgagee does any of these acts, he becomes a transgressor (muta'addi) but the contract remains valid.
The text explicitly states: 'wa la yubtilu 'aqd al-rahn bi al-ta'addi'.
4
Note the Liability Shift
The mortgagee becomes liable for any damage or loss during unauthorized use.
Liability (daman) is imposed due to ta'addi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس له ان يبيع الابتسليط من الراهن وليس له ان يواجر و يعير لانه ليس له ولاية الانتفاع بنفسه فلا یملک تسليط غيره عليه فان فعل كان متعد يا ولا يبطل عقد الرهن بالتعدى
And it is not for him to sell except with authorization from the pawner, and it is not for him to lease or lend because he has no authority over benefiting from it himself, so he cannot authorize someone else over it. So if he does it, he is a transgressor, and the contract of pawn is not invalidated by the transgression.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah. The mortgagee (المرتهن) is prohibited from selling, leasing, or lending the pawned item (المرهون) without the express permission of the pawner (الراهن). The reason given is that the mortgagee himself has no right to use the pawn for his own benefit (only for safekeeping); since he lacks that right, he cannot grant it to others. If he does so anyway, the action is considered transgression (تعدي), but importantly, it does not nullify the pawn contract itself. The contract remains valid, and the pawn continues to be held as security. The liability for damage during such unauthorized use shifts to the mortgagee.

Key Terms
مرتهن (murtahin): The person who receives the pawn as security for a debt (mortgagee).
راهن (rahin): The person who gives the pawn (pawner).
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression: any act by the mortgagee that exceeds the limits of permissible custody, such as using or disposing of the pawn without authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee sells the pawn without the pawner's permission, what is the status of the pawn contract according to the Hanafi school?
A) The contract becomes void immediately
B) The contract remains valid and the mortgagee is a transgressor
C) The contract becomes void only if the pawn is lost
D) The contract is transformed into a sale contract

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's unauthorized disposal of the pawn is haram and constitutes transgression, but it does not invalidate the pawn contract.

With Whom Mortgagee May Entrust the Pawn for Safekeeping
Ruling on whom the mortgagee may delegate safekeeping without liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the persons to whom the mortgagee may delegate safekeeping without liability and explain the consequence of delegation to outsiders.

Core Idea
The mortgagee may treat the pawn like his own deposit: entrust to household, but outsider delegation costs him liability.

In this passage, al-Hidayah clarifies a crucial rule of rahn: the mortgagee is not a mere custodian but a trustee with limited delegation rights. The text draws an elegant qiyas to wadi'ah, showing the Hanafi method of extending a ruling from one trust relationship to another. This lesson unpacks the rule and its underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permitted delegates
List the persons to whom the mortgagee may entrust the pawn without incurring liability: himself, his wife, his child, and his resident servant (those in his iyal).
The child must also be in his household (iyal), not necessarily financially dependent.
2
Understand the legal basis
The pawn in the mortgagee's hand is a trust (amanah), analogous to a deposit (wadi'ah). Just as a depositary may delegate to his household without liability, so may the mortgagee.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the shared illa of amanah.
3
Apply the illa
The effective cause (illa) for permissibility is that both wadi'ah and rahn are trusts in the hands of the holder. The mortgagee's care over the pawn is the same type of custodianship as that of a depositary.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) and extracted via tahqiq al-manat.
4
Identify the prohibition
If the mortgagee entrusts the pawn to someone outside his iyal (e.g., a neighbor, a non-resident employee, or another person), he becomes liable (damin) for any loss.
Liability arises because this is a deviation from the trust's standard care.
5
Note the unresolved difference
Whether the outsider (second receiver) also becomes liable is a matter of ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) already detailed in the chapter of wadi'ah.
This nuance is beyond the scope of this passage; refer to wadi'ah for full treatment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وللمرتهن أن يحفظ الرهن بنفسه وزوجته وولده وخادمه الذى فى عياله قال رضى الله عنه معده ان يكون الولد فى عياله ايضا وهذا لان عينه امانة في يده فصار كا لوديعة وان حفظه بغير من فى عياله او اودعه ضمن وهل يضمن الثاني فهو على الخلاف وقد بينا جميع ذلك بدلائله في الوديعة
He (al-Quduri) said: And it is permissible for the mortgagee to protect the pawn by himself, his wife, his child, and his servant who is in his household. He (the author) said radiyallahu anhu: meaning that the child is also in his household. And this is because the pawned item in his hand is a trust (amanah), so it becomes like a deposit (wadi'ah). And if he protects it with someone other than those in his household or deposits it, he becomes liable (damin). And whether the second person is liable? That is based on the known difference of opinion. And we have explained all that with its proofs in the Book of Deposits.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah, quoting al-Quduri. It clarifies that the mortgagee may delegate the safekeeping of the pawn to himself, his wife, his child, and his servant who lives in his household (those under his care). The rationale is that the pawn is a trust (amanah) in his hands, analogous to a deposit (wadi'ah). If he entrusts it to someone outside this circle, or deposits it elsewhere, he becomes liable for any loss (daman). The question of whether the second party (the outsider) is also liable is a matter of ikhtilaf already discussed in the chapter on deposits. The commentary further explains that the criterion for 'household' is residence, not necessarily financial obligation. Daily wage workers are not included. Also, partners in a joint partnership (shirkat al-mufawada or dirhaman) are treated like household members.

Key Terms
عیال (iyal): Household dependents – those who live in the same house and are under one's care, whether or not he is obligated to support them.
وديعة (wadi'ah): Deposit – an item entrusted to someone for safekeeping without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if a mortgagee gives the pawn for safekeeping to his daily-wage servant who does not live in his house, and the pawn is lost, what is the ruling?
A) The mortgagee is not liable because the servant is in his employment
B) The mortgagee is liable (damin) for the value
C) The servant becomes liable and the mortgagee is free
D) The pawn contract becomes void

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's liability depends on whether he delegates to his household (iyal); delegation to outsiders shifts the risk to him.

Liability of Mortgagee Upon Transgression
Ruling that transgression makes mortgagee liable for full value like usurpation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on mortgagee transgression and explain why the mortgagee becomes liable for the full value of the pawn.

Core Idea
Transgression by the mortgagee turns the pawn into a usurped item, making him liable for its full value.

This lesson examines a key protective rule in the law of pawn (rahn): when the mortgagee oversteps his bounds by using or misusing the pawn, his liability shifts from a trustee (amin) to a usurper (ghasib). The consequence is severe – he must pay the full market value, not just the debt. This rule ensures the pawner's property is safeguarded against abuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'ta'addi' (transgression) by the mortgagee regarding the pawn. The ruling is that he becomes liable (damān) like a usurper for the entire value of the pawn.
Transgression includes using the pawn without permission, misusing it, or failing to safeguard it properly.
2
Understand the reasoning (talīl)
The text gives a reason: because the excess value over the debt is an amānah (trust). Trusts are not normally liable for loss, but transgression breaks that immunity.
The logic is that the pawn secures the debt; the debtor's ownership continues, and the mortgagee holds the surplus in trust.
3
Note the analogy to ghasp
The liability is 'damān al-ghaṣb' – the same as usurpation. This means the mortgagee must pay the highest value from the time of transgression to the time of loss.
Standard Hanafi rule: a usurper is liable for the maximum value during the period of usurpation.
4
Apply the principle
In a real case: if a ring worth 100 is pawned for a debt of 60, and the mortgagee wears the ring (transgression) and it is lost, he must pay 100, not 60.
This protects the pawner's equity beyond the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا تعدى المرتهن فى الرهن ضمنه ضمان الغصب بجميع قيمته لان الزيادة على مقدار الدين امانة والامانات تضمن بالتعدى
And when the mortgagee transgresses regarding the pawn, he becomes liable for it with the liability of usurpation (ghasp) for its entire value, because the excess over the amount of the debt is a trust, and trusts are made liable (guaranteed) by transgression.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah. It states the general principle: if the mortgagee commits any act of transgression (ta'addi) in relation to the pawn, such as using it without permission, he assumes the liability of a usurper (ghasp). This means he must pay the full market value of the pawn if it is lost or damaged, not just the amount of the debt. The reasoning is that the pawn secures the debt; any value above the debt is held in trust for the pawner. A trust normally carries no liability for loss, but transgression breaks that immunity, making the transgressor liable for the entire value, just like a usurper.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Usurpation – wrongfully taking possession of another's property by force or without right. Here, the liability is analogous to that of a usurper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgagee uses a pawned ring without permission and it gets lost, what does he owe according to this passage?
A) Only the amount of the debt
B) The full market value of the ring
C) Nothing, because it was a trust
D) The cost of the ring minus the debt

Key Takeaway
Transgression by the mortgagee transforms his liability from a trustee (only debt) to a usurper (full value), protecting the pawner's equity.

Custom Determines Use vs. Safekeeping of Pawned Items
Ruling distinguishing customary use from safekeeping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of custom to distinguish between permissible safekeeping and transgressive use of a pawned item, and determine liability accordingly.

Core Idea
Custom determines use: only customary wearing of a pawned ring or cloak constitutes use; otherwise it's safekeeping.

In this passage, we see how Hanafi fiqh uses custom (ʿādah) to draw the line between legitimate safekeeping and prohibited use of a pawned item. The mortgagee is permitted only to keep the item safe, not to use it. But what counts as 'use'? Custom provides the answer. By examining the examples of a ring and a cloak, you will learn to apply this principle in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The mortgagee uses a pawned item without the owner's permission. This act is a transgression (taʿaddī) that makes him liable (ḍāmin) if the item is lost or damaged.
The default: permission is for safekeeping only, not use.
2
Recognize the role of custom (ʿādah)
Custom determines whether an action is considered 'use' or 'safekeeping'. The text uses 'al-ʿādah' (العادة) as the criterion.
Custom can vary by time, place, and gender.
3
Apply to the ring example
For men, the only customary finger for wearing a ring is the little finger (al-khinṣir). If the mortgagee puts the ring there, it is use → liability. Putting it on any other finger is not customary, so it is safekeeping → no liability.
Right and left hands are equal; custom may differ for each.
4
Apply to the cloak example
Wearing a cloak draped over the body in the customary manner is use. Placing it on the shoulder (folded) is not customary, so it is safekeeping.
The same principle of custom applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو رهنه خاتما فجعله في خنصره فهو ضامن لانه متعد بالاستعمال لانه غير ما ذون فيه وانما الاذن بالحفظ واليمنى واليسرى في ذلك سواء لان العادة فيه مختلفة ولو جعله في بقية الاصابع كان رهنا بما فيه لانه لا يلبس كذلك عادة فكان من باب الحفظ وكذا الطيلسان ان لبسه لبسا معتادا ضمن وان وضعه على عاتقه لم يضمن
So if he pawns a ring and puts it on his little finger, he is liable (damin) because he is a transgressor by use, because he is not permitted to use it; permission is only for safekeeping. And the right and left hands are equal in this because custom is different in them. And if he puts it on the remaining fingers, it is a pawn with what it contains [i.e., it remains as is] because it is not worn that way customarily, so it is from the category of safekeeping. And likewise, the cloak: if he wears it in a customary manner, he is liable; and if he puts it on his shoulder, he is not liable.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage provides examples to distinguish between use (which constitutes transgression) and safekeeping. The key is custom (عادت). For a ring, the customary wearing is on the little finger (خنصر). If the mortgagee puts it there, it is considered use, making him liable. The right or left hand does not matter because custom varies. If he puts it on any other finger where rings are not customarily worn, that is considered safekeeping (since it is merely placed there for protection), so no liability. Similarly, a cloak: wearing it in the normal way (draped) is use; placing it on the shoulder (like a fold) is safekeeping. The commentary adds that for women, the custom is to wear rings on all fingers, so a female mortgagee would be liable if she wears it on any finger. The ruling is gender-specific based on custom.

Key Terms
خنصر (khinsir): The little finger (pinky). The customary finger for wearing a ring for men.
عادت ('adah): Custom – the prevailing practice that determines whether an action is use or safekeeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man pawns his ring to a male mortgagee. The mortgagee puts the ring on his index finger. The ring is lost. Is the mortgagee liable?
A) Yes, because he wore it at all.
B) No, because wearing on the index finger is not customary for men, so it is considered safekeeping.
C) Yes, because the left and right hands differ.
D) No, because the ring is still secure.

Key Takeaway
Wearing a pawned ring on the little finger (for men) or draping a pawned cloak is use; putting the ring on other fingers or the cloak on the shoulder is safekeeping – custom is the decisive factor.
