Mortgagee's Transgression and Use of Pledge
Ruling on mortgagee liability for transgression and use of pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on mortgagee's transgression and distinguish between permissible preservation and impermissible use based on custom.

Core Idea
The mortgagee's transgression turns trustee into usurper: full value guaranteed.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine a key principle in Hanafi pledge law: the boundary between permissible preservation and impermissible use. The mortgagee holds the excess value as a trust, but transgression forfeits that status. The ruling pivots on custom (urf) to determine whether an action is preservation or use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The mortgagee's transgression (ta'addi) in the pledge triggers a guarantee of the full value, like a usurper.
The ruling is clear: transgression removes trusteeship.
2
Locate the dalil
What is the proof? The text states the excess over the debt is a trust, and trusts are guaranteed by transgression. This is a qiyas analogizing to other trusts.
The excess (amanah) is the key element.
3
Apply to the ring example
Wearing the ring on the little finger (khinsir) is customary use for men, so it is transgression. Other fingers are not customary, so it is preservation.
Custom defines use.
4
Apply to the cloak example
Wearing the cloak in a customary manner is use (transgression); placing it on the shoulder is preservation (no transgression).
Same principle: custom differentiates.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is that any transgression (even if no actual loss) makes the mortgagee liable for full value. The examples clarify the boundary.
The ruling is operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا تعدى المرتهن فى الرهن ضمنه ضمان الغصب بجميع قيمته لان الزيادة على مقدار الدين امانة والامانات تضمن بالتعدى
فلو رهنه خاتما فجعله في خنصره فهو ضامن لانه متعد بالاستعمال لانه غير ما ذون فيه وانما الاذن بالحفظ واليمنى واليسرى في ذلك سواء لان العادة فيه مختلفة ولو جعله في بقية الاصابع كان رهنا بما فيه لانه لا يلبس كذلك عادة فكان من باب الحفظ وكذا الطيلسان ان لبسه لبسا معتادا ضمن وان وضعه على عاتقه لم يضمن
If the mortgagee transgresses in the pledge, he guarantees it with the guarantee of usurpation for its entire value, because the excess over the amount of the debt is a trust, and trusts are guaranteed by transgression. So if he pledged a ring and he put it on his little finger, he is a guarantor because he is transgressing by use, because he is not permitted to use it; permission is only for preservation. The right and left hand are the same in this, because custom differs. If he put it on the remaining fingers, it remains a pledge with what is in it, because it is not worn customarily like that, so it is from the category of preservation. Similarly, the cloak: if he wears it in a customary manner, he guarantees; if he places it on his shoulder, he does not guarantee.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage states a ruling with its rationale. The mortgagee (murtahin) is a trustee (amin) for the pledged property beyond the debt amount, but transgression (ta'addi) converts his liability to that of a usurper (ghasib), making him liable for the full value. The proof is that the excess is an amanah, and trusteeship is lost through transgression. The example of a ring clarifies use vs. preservation: wearing on the little finger (khinsir) is customary use for men, so liability; other fingers are not customary, so it is preservation. The same applies to a cloak: wearing it is use, placing on shoulder is preservation. For women, all fingers are customary, so any wearing incurs liability.

Key Terms
تعدى (ta'addi): Transgression or misuse by the mortgagee against the terms of the pledge.
خنصر (khinsir): The little finger, the customary finger for wearing a ring for men.
ضمان الغصب (daman al-ghasb): Liability akin to usurpation, requiring compensation of the full value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he used it.
B) No, because it is not customary use, so it is preservation.
C) Yes, because any finger constitutes use.
D) No, because the mortgagee is always exempt.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's liability turns on whether his action is transgression (use) or preservation, as determined by custom (urf).

Hanging Pledged Swords Around the Neck
Ruling on liability when mortgagee hangs pledged swords around neck

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that custom ('urf) distinguishes use from preservation in pledges and state the liability consequence.

Core Idea
Custom determines liability in pledges: customary use triggers guarantee; non-customary action is preservation.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school on pledges: does the mortgagee's action of wearing pledged swords trigger liability? The answer depends on what is customary among warriors. This demonstrates how custom ('urf) functions as a legal indicator in mu'amalat, distinguishing permissible handling that preserves the pledge from use that incurs liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the pledged items
The mortgagee wears two or three swords hung from his neck.
The act is the same: taqallud (wearing hanging).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For two swords: liable (daman wajib). For three swords: not liable.
The difference hinges on custom.
3
Extract the effective cause (illa)
The illa is customary practice ('urf): wearing two swords is customary for warriors in war; wearing three is not.
Custom defines what constitutes 'use' as opposed to mere preservation.
4
Apply the principle
If the action is customary for that type of item, it is use, and the mortgagee is liable. If not, it is preservation, and no liability.
This prevents arbitrary liability while protecting the pledgor's rights.
5
Note the authority
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.
No known intra-Hanafi or cross-madhhab ikhtilaf on this specific issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو رهنه سيفين اوثلثة فتقلدها لم يضمن فى الثلثة وضمن فى السيفين لان العادة جرت بين الشجعان بتقلد سيفين في الحرب ولم تجر بتقلد الثالثة
If he pledged two or three swords and he wore them hanging [from the neck], he does not guarantee in the case of three, and he guarantees in the case of two, because custom prevails among the brave of wearing two swords in war, but wearing a third is not customary.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on distinguishing use from preservation based on custom ('urf). For pledged swords, wearing two swords around the neck is customary among warriors in battle, so it constitutes use, making the mortgagee liable. Wearing three swords is not customary, so it is considered preservation, and no liability arises. The illa (effective cause) is the customary practice; custom differentiates between use and mere holding.

Key Terms
تقلد (taqallud): Wearing something (like a sword) hanging from the neck or shoulder.
عادة ('adah): Customary practice that distinguishes use from preservation in pledges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Mortgagee Wearing Two Rings: Custom Determines Liability
Ruling on mortgagee wearing two rings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mortgagee wearing two rings on one finger and determine liability based on the custom of adornment.

Core Idea
Custom decides whether wearing two rings is use (liable) or preservation (not liable).

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario within the chapter of rahn (pledge): the mortgagee places the pledged ring on top of his existing ring. The ruling hinges not on the mere act of wearing, but on whether the mortgagee customarily does so for adornment. This shows how custom ('urf) functions as a decisive factor in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is the mortgagee wearing a pledged ring on top of another ring on the same finger. Determine what fiqh issue it raises: is this an act of use (intifa') or preservation (hifz)?
2
State the ruling based on custom
The text presents two cases: if the mortgagee is known to adorn himself with two rings, it counts as use and he is liable (daman). If not, it counts as preservation and no liability.
3
Identify the 'illa (effective cause)
The 'illa is the customary practice of adornment (yatajammalu). Custom distinguishes between use and preservation. This 'illa is extracted from the text's conditional phrasing.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a mortgagee who never wears two rings. He adds the pledged ring for safety. Since he does not adorn himself that way, the act is preservation, and he is not liable.
5
Note the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that custom determines the ruling, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah. No intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان لبس خاتما فوق خاتم ان كان هو ممن يتجمل بلبس خاتمين ضمن وان كان لا يتجمل بذلك فهو حافظ فلا يضمن
If he wears a ring over a ring, if he is one who adorns himself by wearing two rings, he guarantees; if he does not adorn himself by that, then he is a preserver and so does not guarantee.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides another example where custom determines liability. If the mortgagee wears a pledged ring on top of another ring (on the same finger), the ruling depends on whether he customarily does so for adornment. If he is known to wear two rings for beauty, it is use and he guarantees; if not, it is preservation. The 'illa is the customary practice of adornment.

Key Terms
يتجمل (yatajammalu): To adorn or beautify oneself, i.e., wearing rings for decoration.

Allocating Expenses in Rahn: The Hanafi Principle
Ruling on who bears expenses for preserving the pledged property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle for allocating expenses on a pledged property by distinguishing between storage costs (on mortgagee) and maintenance costs (on mortgagor).

Core Idea
Mortgagee bears storage; mortgagor bears upkeep—ownership determines responsibility.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies how expenses for a pledged property (rahn) are allocated between mortgagee (murtahin) and mortgagor (rahin). The underlying principle is that the owner (mortgagor) bears all costs related to the property's benefit and preservation, while the mortgagee bears only those directly linked to keeping the property safe. Understanding this allocation is essential for practitioners of Islamic finance and for avoiding disputes in pawn contracts.

Guided Path
1
Extract the specific rulings
List the expenses mentioned and which party bears each: mortgagee bears house rent, guard wages, shepherd wages; mortgagor bears food and drink (nafaqa).
Note that shepherd wages are initially placed on mortgagee but later equated to feeding—highlighting the nuance.
2
State the general principle (al-asl)
Locate the sentence: 'the principle is that what is needed for the benefit and preservation of the pledge is on the mortgagor.' Rewrite it in your own words.
This principle governs all such expenses.
3
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is ownership: the substance (ayn) and usufructs (manafi‘) belong to the mortgagor, so he must bear the burden of preservation. The passage analogizes to deposit (wadi‘ah).
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Distinguish between hifz (safeguarding) and ibqa' (preserving existence)
Storage costs (house, guard) are for safeguarding (hifz) the property, and these fall on the mortgagee as the custodian. Maintenance costs (food, drink) are for preserving the property's existence (ibqa'), and these fall on the owner (mortgagor).
Shepherd wages straddle both: guarding (hifz) and feeding (ibqa'). The text resolves this by treating it as feeding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واجرة البيت الذى يحفظ فيه الرهن على المرتهن وكذلك اجرة الحافظ واجرة الراعى ونفقة الرهن على الراهن والاصل ان ما يحتاج اليه لمصلحة الرهن وتبقيته فهو على الراهن سواء كان في الرهن فضل اولم يكن لان العين باق على ملكه وكذلك منافعه مملوكة له فيكون صلاحه وتبقيته عليه لما انه مؤنة ملکه کما في الوديعة وذلك مثل النفقة فى ماكله ومشربه واجرة الراعي في معناه لانه علف الحيوان
He said: The rent of the house in which the pledge is kept is on the mortgagee, and similarly the wages of the guard and the wages of the shepherd, and the maintenance of the pledge is on the mortgagor. The principle is that what is needed for the benefit and preservation of the pledge is on the mortgagor, whether there is surplus in the pledge or not, because the substance remains in his ownership, and similarly its usufructs are owned by him. So its betterment and preservation are upon him, as it is the burden of his property, just as in a deposit. That includes expenses for its food and drink, and the wages of the shepherd are in its meaning, because it is feeding the animal.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage lays down a general principle (asl) for allocating expenses related to a pledged property. The mortgagee bears costs directly linked to storage and guarding (house, guard, shepherd wages) because these are for preservation. The mortgagor bears costs for maintenance (nafaqa) like food and drink, because ownership remains with him. The analogy to deposit (wadi'ah) is drawn: the owner bears maintenance, the custodian bears storage. The 'illa is ownership of the property and its benefits.

Key Terms
مؤنة (mu'nah): The financial burden or expense required for upkeep.
نفقة (nafaqa): Maintenance expenses, especially food and drink for animals.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mortgagee bears storage costs (house, guard, shepherd) while the mortgagor bears maintenance costs (food, drink), based on the principle that ownership determines responsibility for preservation.

General Principle of Expenses in Rahn
Establishes a general rule for expense allocation in rahn with examples and a qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for expenses in a rahn contract and apply it to distinguish between preservation expenses (on the mortgagee) and maintenance expenses (on the mortgagor).

Core Idea
In rahn, the mortgagee bears preservation costs; the mortgagor bears maintenance costs.

When property is mortgaged, it is held by the mortgagee, but ownership remains with the mortgagor. This often raises the question: who pays for the various expenses? The Hanafi school provides a clear dividing line based on the nature of each expense. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly allocating costs and avoiding disputes in Islamic finance and everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of expense
The rule splits expenses into two categories: preservation (hifazat) – costs to keep the property safe, and maintenance/improvement (islah wa ibqa') – costs to keep the property in good condition and productive.
Preservation benefits the mortgagee who holds the property; maintenance benefits the owner who retains ownership.
2
Apply the rule to standard examples
Using the examples from the text: rent of storage and watchman's wages are preservation, so on the mortgagee. Food, clothing, and shepherd's wages are maintenance, so on the mortgagor.
3
Analyze the shepherd question via qiyas
The text raises an objection: a shepherd both grazes (maintenance) and guards (preservation). The Hanafi response uses qiyas: theft from an open pasture does not incur the hadd penalty because it is not a protected place, proving that grazing (maintenance) is primary. Therefore, the entire wage is on the mortgagor.
This shows how legal reasoning (qiyas) resolves apparent overlaps between categories.
4
Consider the detailed list of maintenance expenses
The author specifies additional maintenance items from the matn: clothing of slaves, wages of a wet nurse for a child of a mortgaged female slave, irrigation, digging canals, pollination, harvesting, and all other necessary tasks for the property's upkeep. All are on the mortgagor.
The list is illustrative, not exhaustive; the principle extends to similar expenses.

کا عین راہن کی ملکیت ہے اور منافع مرہون بھی راہن کی ملکیت ہے اور ملکیت کے لئے جو چیز اصلاح و ابقاء کے واسطے ہوتی ہے وہ مالک کے ذمہ واجب ہوتی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ خالص ودیعت میں بھی اصلاح و ابقاء کی چیزیں مالک کے ذمہ ہوتی ہیں۔ سوال: راعی جس طریقہ سے حیوان کو چراتا ہے اور اس کی حفاظت بھی کرتا ہے لہذا راعی کی اجرت دونوں پر ہونی چاہیے؟ جواب: راعی کا مقصد اصلی چرانا ہے جو اصلاح و ابقاء کے باب سے ہے اور حفاظت ضمنی چیز ہے اس لئے راعی کی پوری اجرت راہن کے ذمہ ہوگی۔ سوال: اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ راعی کا مقصد اصلی حفاظت نہیں ہے؟ جواب: اگر کوئی چراگاہ میں سے جانور کو چرالے تو اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا اگر والقيام بمصالحه اور اسی جنس سے ( یعنی اصلاح و ابقاء کی جنس سے ) ہے غلام کے کپڑے اور مرہون کے بچہ کے لئے مرضعہ کی اجرت اور باغ کو سیراب کرنا اور نہر کھودنا اور باغ کے درختوں میں مادہ پر نر کا شگوفہ ڈالنا اور اس کے پھل توڑنا اور اس کے دیگر مصالح کیلئے قائم رہنا۔ تشریح: جن چیزوں کا شمار اصلاح و ابقاء کے باب سے ہے مصنف ان میں سے کچھ امور کی نشاندہی فرمارہے ہیں: (۱) غلام کے کپڑے بھی اسی جنس سے ہیں تو اس کو سیراب کرنا راہن کا فریضہ ہوگا۔ (۴) اگر باغ کو سیراب کرنے کے لئے نہر کھودنے کی ضرورت ہو تو یہ کام بھی راہن کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ (۵) مادہ درختوں پر نر درختوں کے شگوفے ڈالنے کا کام بھی راہن کے ذمہ ہوگا اس تلقیح کو تا بیر کہتے ہیں اور یہ جائز ہے اور باذن اللہ تا بیر سے پھل زیادہ آتا ہے۔ (۶) باغ کا پھل توڑنا بھی راہن کا فریضہ ہوگا۔ (۷) اور اس کے علاوہ جتنی بھی وہ امور ہیں کہ باغ کی اصلاح و ابقاء کے لئے جو ضروری ہیں وہ سب راہن کے ذمہ ہوں گے، خواہ خود کرے یا مزدور سے کرائے۔
Explanation: It has passed earlier that the mortgaged property remains detained with the mortgagee. Now a question arises: whose responsibility is its maintenance, the rent of the place where it is kept, and the wages of the watchman? For this, a general principle has been stated: whatever pertains to preservation is the responsibility of the mortgagee, and whatever pertains to improvement and maintenance is the responsibility of the mortgagor. This principle applies regardless of whether the value of the collateral is greater than, equal to, or less than the debt. Therefore, the rent of the room and the wages of the watchman are obligatory on the mortgagee. The wages of the shepherd, the maintenance of the collateral, and its clothing are all on the mortgagor. The reason is that the substance of the collateral is owned by the mortgagor, and its profits are also owned by the mortgagor. Whatever is for improvement and maintenance of ownership is obligatory on the owner. For the same reason, in a pure deposit, items for improvement and maintenance are on the owner. Question: The shepherd both grazes and protects the animal, so his wages should be on both? Answer: The shepherd's primary purpose is grazing, which is from improvement and maintenance, and protection is incidental; thus the entire wage is on the mortgagor. Question: What is the proof that protection is not the primary purpose? Answer: If someone steals the animal from the pasture, his hand is not cut off; if the shepherd were a guardian, the hand would be cut off for stealing from a protected place. What things are from the category of improvement and maintenance? And from this category are: clothing of slaves, wages of a wet nurse for the child of the mortgaged property, irrigating the orchard, digging the canal, pollinating its palm trees, harvesting, and undertaking its maintenance. Explanation: The author indicates some matters that are counted from the category of improvement and maintenance: (1) Clothing of slaves is from this category, so it is on the mortgagor. (2) If a female slave is mortgaged and she gives birth, and the slave does not produce milk, then the wages of a wet nurse hired for the child are on the mortgagor. (3) If an orchard is mortgaged, irrigating it is the duty of the mortgagor. (4) If digging a canal is needed to irrigate the orchard, that is also on the mortgagor. (5) Pollinating female date palms with male flowers is also on the mortgagor; this is called ta'bir and it is permissible, and by the permission of Allah, pollination increases fruit. (6) Harvesting the fruit of the orchard is also the duty of the mortgagor. (7) And besides these, whatever matters are necessary for the improvement and maintenance of the orchard are all on the mortgagor, whether he does it himself or hires a worker.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage states a key legal rule for rahn (pawn/pledge) regarding expenses. The rule divides expenses into two categories: (1) expenses of preservation (hifazah) which fall on the mortgagee (murtahin) because he has the right of detention, and (2) expenses of maintenance and improvement (islah wa ibqa') which fall on the mortgagor (rahin) because he owns the property and its profits. The passage then applies this rule to several examples: the rent of storage and watchman's wages are preservation expenses, so the mortgagee pays; the shepherd's wages, food, and clothing are maintenance expenses, so the mortgagor pays. A question about the shepherd is resolved by noting that grazing (maintenance) is the primary purpose, not guarding (preservation), as indicated by the fact that theft from an open pasture does not incur the hadd penalty for theft (cutting of hand), whereas theft from a guarded place would. The author then provides a list of expenses from the matn that are considered maintenance: clothing of slaves, wages of a wet nurse for the offspring of a mortgaged slave, irrigation, digging canals, pollination, harvesting, and other similar tasks. All these are on the mortgagor, regardless of whether he performs them personally or hires workers. The ruling is straightforward: the mortgagee bears costs of keeping the property safe, while the owner bears costs of keeping it productive and in good condition.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract where property is held as security for a debt
مرہون (marhun): The property that is mortgaged as collateral
راہن (rahin): The person who pledges property as security (mortgagor)
مرتہن (murtahin): The person who receives the pledge (mortgagee)
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance expenses such as food and clothing
حفاظت (hifazat): Preservation and guarding of the mortgaged property
اصلاح و ابقاء (islah wa ibqa'): Improvement and maintenance to keep the property in good condition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, expenses in a rahn contract are divided by their nature: preservation costs on the mortgagee, maintenance costs on the mortgagor, regardless of the collateral's value relative to the debt.

Preservation Expenses in Rahn: Mortgagee vs Mortgagor
States the Zahir al-Riwayah rule for preservation expenses and records Abu Yusuf's contrary view on storage rent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on preservation expenses in rahn and distinguish Imam Abu Yusuf's intra-madhhab dispute on storage rent.

Core Idea
Preservation costs fall on the mortgagee; but Abu Yusuf places storage rent on the mortgagor like maintenance.

A mortgagee holds the collateral as security. Naturally, preserving that collateral costs money – guards, storage, treatment. Who bears these costs? This passage from al-Hidayah gives the default Hanafi rule and reports a minority intra-madhhab view from Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this distinction clarifies the broader principle: preservation follows the right to detain (imsak), while maintenance remains on the owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that every expense for preserving the collateral, returning it, or returning a part of it is on the mortgagee. Examples: wages of a guard, rent of the storage house.
This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah – the relied-upon transmission.
2
Understand the legal basis (talil)
The mortgagee has the right to detain (imsak) the collateral; preservation is a necessary consequence of that right. Therefore, its compensation falls on him.
The logic: right → duty → liability for costs.
3
Recognize the exception (Abu Yusuf's view)
Imam Abu Yusuf, in a Nawadir (rare) transmission, holds that the rent of the dwelling (storage house) is on the mortgagor, analogizing it to maintenance (nafaqah), which is always on the owner.
His analogy: both maintenance and storage rent aim to keep the property existing (saiy fi tabqiyatihi).
4
Contrast preservation vs maintenance
The general rule distinguishes preservation (hifazah) – on mortgagee – from maintenance (nafaqah) – on owner. Abu Yusuf blurs this line for storage rent.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical consequence of who pays storage rent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the Zahir al-Riwayah rule: preservation expenses, including storage rent, are on the mortgagee. Abu Yusuf's view is recorded but not operative.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah > Nawadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ما كان لحفظه أو رده إلى يد المرتهن أو رد جزء منه فهو على المرتهن مثل أجرة الحافظ لأن الإمساك حق له والحفظ واجب عليه فيكون بدله عليه وكذلك أجرة البيت الذي يحفظ الرهن فيه وهذا في ظاهر الرواية. ترجمہ: اور ہر کام جو مرہون کی حفاظت کیلئے ہو یا اس کو مرتہن کی جانب واپس کرنے کے لئے ہو یا اس کے کسی اجزاء کو واپس کرنے کے لئے ہو وہ مرتہن کے ذمہ ہے جیسے نگراں کی اجرت اس لئے کہ امساک (حبس) مرتہن کا حق ہے اور حفاظت کرنا مرتہن پر واجب ہے تو حفاظت کا عوض مرتہن پر ہوگا اور ایسے ہی اس گھر کی اجرت جس میں رہن کی حفاظت کی جائے اور یہ ظاہر الروایہ میں ہے۔ تشریح: جو کام از باب حفاظت ہو وہ مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوتا ہے اور اگر مرہون بھاگ جائے تو اس کی واپسی بھی از باب حفاظت ہے لہذا واپس لانا یا اس کی مزدوری بھی مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگی اسی طرح اگر مرہون بیمار ہو جائے تو اس کا علاج معالجہ گویا کہ اس کے جزء کی واپسی ہے لہذا یہ بھی مرتہن کے ذمہ ہے اسی طرح نگراں کی اجرت بھی مرتہن کے ذمہ ہے کیونکہ یہ از باب حفاظت ہے اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو مرہون کے امساک و حبس کا حق ہے تو حفاظت بھی اسی کے ذمہ ضروری ہوگی لہذا حفاظت کی جائے اس کا کرایہ بھی مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگا اور یہ ظاہر الروایہ ہے۔ وعن أبي يوسف أن كراء الماوى على الراهن بمنزلة النفقة لأنه سعي في تبقيته. ترجمہ: اور ابو یوسف سے (نوادر میں) منقول ہے کہ مکان کا کرایہ راہن پر ہو گا نفقہ کے درجہ میں اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے باقی رکھنے میں کوشش کرنا ہے۔ تشریح: امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ مکان کا کرایہ راہن کے ذمہ ہو گا جیسے نفقہ راہن کے ذمہ ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جس طرح نفقہ از باب ابقاء ہے اسی طرح مکان کا کرایہ بھی ابقاء کے لئے ہے۔
And everything that is for its preservation or returning it to the hand of the mortgagee or returning a part of it is upon the mortgagee, like the wages of the guardian, because detention is his right and preservation is obligatory upon him, so its compensation is upon him. Similarly, the rent of the house in which the collateral is kept, and this is in Zahir al-Riwayah. Explanation: Whatever work is from the category of preservation is upon the mortgagee. If the collateral runs away, returning it is also from preservation, so bringing it back or its wages are upon the mortgagee. Similarly, if the collateral becomes sick, its treatment is like returning a part of it, so it is also upon the mortgagee. Likewise, the wages of the guardian are upon the mortgagee because this is from preservation, since the mortgagee has the right to detain the collateral, so preservation is also incumbent upon him, so the rent for its preservation is upon the mortgagee. And this is in Zahir al-Riwayah. And from Abu Yusuf: that the rent of the dwelling is upon the mortgagor, like maintenance, because it is an effort to keep it remaining. Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf says that the rent of the house is upon the mortgagor, just as maintenance is upon the mortgagor, because just as maintenance is from preservation, similarly the rent of the house is also for preservation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for preservation expenses (hifazah) in a rahn contract. The matn (from Hidayah) states a general rule: any expense required for preserving the collateral, returning it to the mortgagee, or returning a part of it (e.g., if an animal runs away or becomes ill and needs treatment) is on the mortgagee. The examples given are the wages of a guard and the rent of a storage place. The commentary explains that the mortgagee has the right to detain the collateral, so preservation is his duty, and thus its costs fall on him. This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon transmission of Imam Muhammad). However, Imam Abu Yusuf, in a Nawadir (rare transmission), differs: he considers the rent of a dwelling to be like maintenance (nafaqah) and thus on the mortgagor, because it is an effort to keep the property existing. The commentary notes that Abu Yusuf analogizes rent to maintenance, as both serve to preserve the property. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Zahir al-Riwayah view (on the mortgagee), but the difference is recorded. The passage highlights that while maintenance (nafaqah) is clearly on the owner, preservation costs are on the mortgagee by default.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative transmissions of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six core books
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less known transmissions, such as those of Hasan ibn Ziyad or Abu Yusuf's solitary reports
امساک (imsak): The right of the mortgagee to detain the mortgaged property
اجرت الحافظ (ujrat al-hafiz): Wages of a guardian or watchman for the collateral

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, who is responsible for paying rent for the house where a mortgaged item is stored?
A) The mortgagor (rahin) because he owns the item
B) The mortgagee (murtahin) because it is a preservation expense
C) Both equally since both benefit from storage
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
Preservation costs in rahn fall on the mortgagee due to his right to detain; storage rent is similarly on him per the relied-upon view, while maintenance remains on the owner.

Maintenance vs. Protection Expenses in Rahn
General rule distinguishing maintenance and protection costs between mortgagor and mortgagee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between maintenance expenses (on the mortgagor) and protection expenses (on the mortgagee) in a rahn contract and apply the rule to novel cases.

Core Idea
In rahn, the mortgagor bears maintenance costs; the mortgagee bears protection costs – because the right to hold implies the duty to protect.

This lesson draws a fundamental distinction in the law of mortgage (rahn) between two types of expenses: those that preserve and improve the pawn (maintenance) and those that safeguard it (protection). The Hanafi school allocates these costs differently based on the nature of the obligation. Understanding this rule is crucial for correctly determining financial responsibility in a mortgage arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
First, understand that expenses fall into maintenance (islah wa ibqa) and protection (hifz). The passage lists specific examples for each.
Maintenance includes irrigation, pollination, fruit picking. Protection includes guard wages and house rent.
2
Recognize the default rule
The general rule: everything for protection or returning the pawn (or part of it) to the mortgagee is on the mortgagee. Everything else (improvement/preservation) is on the mortgagor.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The mortgagee has the right to hold (imsaak). Since protection is obligatory on him, the cost of protection (e.g., guard wage) is on him. The mortgagor retains ownership, so he bears costs that maintain the pawn's value.
The text says: 'al-imsaak haqq lahu wa al-hifz wajib alayhi'.
4
Apply to new scenarios
Consider a run-away pawn or a sick pawn. The mortgagee must bear the cost of recovery and treatment because these are protective acts (returning the pawn or its part).
The commentary explicitly extends the rule to these cases.
5
Note the authority level
This is the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah. Note that Imam Abu Yusuf differs on house rent (considered a protective expense in Zahir al-Riwayah but he puts it on the mortgagor).
The difference is from Nawadir, but the mufta bihi in most later works is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Source Text

الروایہ ہے۔
If a garden is mortgaged, then irrigating it is the duty of the mortgagor. 199. 4. If for irrigating the garden it is necessary to dig a canal, then this work is also on the mortgagor. Kitab al-Rahn. The work of grafting male flowers onto female trees is also on the mortgagor; this pollination is called 'tabeer' and it is permissible, and by Allah's permission, more fruit comes from tabeer. Picking the fruit of the garden is also the duty of the mortgagor. And besides this, all other matters that are necessary for the improvement and maintenance of the garden are all on the mortgagor, whether he does them himself or hires a worker. Whatever work is for protection is on the mortgagee. And everything that is for its protection or returning it to the mortgagee's hand or returning a part of it is on the mortgagee, like the wage of a guard, because holding is a right for him and protection is obligatory on him, so its compensation is on him. Similarly, the rent of the house in which the pawn is kept. And this is in Zahir al-Riwayah. Translation: And every work that is for the protection of the pawn or for returning it to the mortgagee's side or for returning any of its parts is on the mortgagee, like the wage of a guard, because holding (detaining) is a right of the mortgagee, and protection is obligatory on the mortgagee, so the compensation for protection is on the mortgagee. Similarly, the rent of the house in which the pawn is protected, and this is in Zahir al-Riwayah. Explanation: Whatever work is for protection is on the mortgagee. And if the pawn runs away, its return is also for protection, so bringing it back or its wage is also on the mortgagee. Similarly, if the pawn becomes sick, its treatment is like returning a part of it, so this is also on the mortgagee. Similarly, the wage of a guard is also on the mortgagee because this is for protection, because the mortgagee has the right to hold and detain the pawn, so protection is also necessary on him, so the rent for protection is also on the mortgagee, and this is in Zahir al-Riwayah.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that distinguishes between two categories of expenses related to a mortgaged property (rahn): those for maintenance and improvement (islah wa ibqa) and those for protection (hifazat). The author begins by enumerating specific works that fall on the rahn (mortgagor): irrigating the garden, digging a canal for irrigation, pollinating trees, picking fruit, and any other work necessary for the preservation and improvement of the garden. These are considered acts that preserve the pawn itself and are therefore the responsibility of the owner (mortgagor). Then the text introduces the general rule for protective works: everything that is for the protection of the pawn or for returning it (or a part of it) to the mortgagee's possession is on the mortgagee (murtaheen). The example given is the wage of a guard (ajrat al-hafiz). The reasoning (ta'lil) provided is that the right to hold (imsaak) belongs to the mortgagee, and protection is obligatory (wajib) upon him, so the compensation (badal) for that protection falls on him. Similarly, the rent for a house where the pawn is stored is also on the mortgagee. The text explicitly states that this ruling is in Zahir al-Riwayah, indicating it is the authoritative transmitted position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary adds that this includes bringing back a runaway slave or treating a sick pawn, both of which are protective acts. Thus, the mortgagee bears all costs of safeguarding the pawn, while the mortgagor bears all costs of maintaining and improving it.

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): Mortgage; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.
مرتہن (murtaheen): The mortgagee (creditor) who holds the pawn as security.
راهن (raahin): The mortgagor (debtor) who gives the pawn.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagor (raahin)
B) The mortgagee (murtaheen)
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In a rahn contract, maintenance costs fall on the mortgagor (owner), while protection costs fall on the mortgagee (holder) due to his duty to safeguard the pawn.

Abu Yusuf's View on House Rent in Rahn
Intra-Hanafi dispute from Nawadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Yusuf's view on house rent in rahn and explain its analogy to maintenance (nafaqah).

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf equates house rent to maintenance — responsibility falls on the mortgagor.

In the previous lesson, you learned the Zahir al-Riwayah position that the mortgagee pays the rent of a house used to store the pawn. Now, we examine an alternative view from Imam Abu Yusuf, recorded in the Nawadir. This lesson shows how a founding imam can differ from the transmitted position, and how the school accommodates such differences without undermining its core doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific legal question? It is: who bears the rent of a dwelling when a pawn is kept there?
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Recall from the previous lesson: the mortgagee pays because he has the right to hold and must protect the pawn.
This is the mufta bihi view.
3
State Abu Yusuf's view
Imam Abu Yusuf says the rent is on the mortgagor, analogous to maintenance (nafaqah).
This is a Nawadir transmission.
4
Analyze the analogy
Why does Abu Yusuf compare rent to maintenance? Both are expenses for preserving the pawn. Maintenance (food, shelter for a living pawn) is always on the owner (mortgagor). By qiyas, house rent for preservation should also be on the mortgagor.
5
Determine the operational ruling
The legitimate ikhtilaf exists, but the school relies on Zahir al-Riwayah. The mufta bihi is that the mortgagee pays.
Abu Yusuf's view is known but not operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابو یوسف کا نقطہ نظر
وعن ابى يوسف ان كراء الماوى على الراهن بمنزلة النفقة لانه سعي في تبقيته ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے ( نوادر میں ) منقول ہے کہ مکان کا کرایہ راہن پر ہو گا نفقہ کے درجہ میں اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے باقی رکھنے میں کوشش کرنا ہے۔ تشریح امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ مکان کا کرایہ راہن کے ذمہ ہو گا جیسے نفقہ راہن کے ذمہ ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جس طرح نفقہ از باب اصلاح و ابقاء ہے اسی طرح مکان بھی از باب اصلاح و ابقاء ہے۔
Imam Abu Yusuf's point of view. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the rent of the dwelling is on the mortgagor like maintenance, because it is an effort in preserving it. Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf (in Nawadir) that the rent of the house is on the mortgagor like maintenance, because it is an effort in preserving it. Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf says that the rent of the house is on the mortgagor, just as maintenance is on the mortgagor, because just as maintenance is from the category of improvement and preservation, similarly the house rent is also from the category of improvement and preservation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. The author records Imam Abu Yusuf's view, transmitted in Nawadir (rare transmissions), regarding the rent of a house used to store the pawn. While the Zahir al-Riwayah (presented in the previous lesson) places the house rent on the mortgagee (murtaheen) because it is a protective expense, Imam Abu Yusuf analogizes it to maintenance (nafaqah), which is on the mortgagor (raahin). His reasoning is that providing a dwelling for the pawn contributes to its preservation and improvement (islah wa ibqa), much like feeding or sheltering a living pawn. The commentary notes that this is a valid position within the school, but it is not the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view from Zahir al-Riwayah. This illustrates how Hanafi fiqh accommodates valid ikhtilaf among the founding imams.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawadir): Rare transmissions in the Hanafi school, as opposed to Zahir al-Riwayah.
ابو یوسف (Abu Yusuf): Imam Abu Yusuf al-Ansari (d. 182 AH), a founding Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food and lodging, typically on the owner of a living pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The mortgagor
C) Both share equally
D) It is a voluntary expense

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's view on house rent in rahn is a valid intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position placing rent on the mortgagee.

Who Bears the Cost of Returning a Runaway Mortgaged Slave?
Rule on who bears the cost (ja'l) of returning a runaway mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the apportioned ja'l for a runaway mortgaged slave when the pawn's value exceeds the debt, applying the Hanafi proportional rule.

Core Idea
The ja'l is split proportionally when the pawn's value exceeds the secured debt.

In this lesson, you will learn the rule on who bears the cost (ja'l) of returning a runaway slave that has been pawned. The default ruling places the full ja'l on the mortgagee when the slave's value equals the debt. However, when the slave's value exceeds the debt, the excess is held as a trust (amanah), so the ja'l is shared proportionally. This ruling is distinguished from the case of house rent, where the entire rent remains on the mortgagee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is returning a runaway pawned slave. The ruling: the ja'l (reward) is wajib on the mortgagee (murtaheen).
2
Recognize the default condition
The default condition is that the pawn's value equals the debt. In that case, the full ja'l falls on the mortgagee because he needs to restore his right of execution.
3
Apply the exception for excess value
When the pawn's value exceeds the debt, the excess is an amanah (trust) held by the mortgagee. Therefore, the ja'l is apportioned: the mortgagee pays a proportion equal to (debt/value), and the mortgagor pays the rest.
The mortgagee is like a depositary over the excess.
4
Calculate the apportionment
Given pawn's value (V), debt (D), and ja'l (J), mortgagee's share = (D/V) * J; mortgagor's share = ((V-D)/V) * J.
Example: V=200, D=150, J=40 => mortgagee pays 30, mortgagor pays 10.
5
Contrast with the house rent case
Unlike ja'l, the entire rent for a pawned house is on the mortgagee even if the house value exceeds the debt, because rent is a periodic expense for protection, not a one-time recovery cost.
This distinction shows the subtlety of Hanafi fiqh in different contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مضمون
و ان كانت قيمة الرهن اكثر فعليه بقدر المضمون وعلى الراهن بقدر الزيادة عليه لانه امانة في يده والرد لاعادة اليد ويده في الزيادة يد المالك اذهو كالمودع فيها فلهذا يكون على المالك

ایک اشکال کا جواب
و هذا بخلاف اجرة البيت الذي ذكرناه فإن كان كلها تجب على المرتهن وان كان في قيمة الرهن فضل
The wage for returning a runaway mortgaged slave is on the mortgagee. And from this category is the ja'l of the runaway slave, for it is on the mortgagee because he is in need of restoring the hand of execution that he had, so that he may return him, so it is from the expense of return, so it is binding on him. And this is when the value of the pawn and the debt are equal. Translation: And from this category is the ja'l of the runaway, so it is on the mortgagee because the mortgagee needs to restore the hand of execution that he had, so that he may return the pawn to the mortgagor, so this is from the expense of return, so it binds him. And this (obligation of ja'l on the mortgagee) is when the debt and the value of the pawn are equal. Explanation: If a slave runs away, the wage for bringing him back is called ja'l... It is learned that bringing back a runaway slave is from the category of protection, so the wage is on the mortgagee, but the full ja'l is obligatory on the mortgagee only when the pawn's value and the debt are equal. Otherwise, if the pawn's value is more, then the ruling is different: the mortgagee is liable to the extent of the secured amount, and the mortgagor is liable for the excess. And if the pawn's value is more, then on him (the mortgagee) to the extent of the secured amount, and on the mortgagor to the extent of the excess, because the excess is an amanah in his hand, and the return is for restoring the hand, and his hand over the excess is the hand of the owner, for he is like a depositary over it, so for this reason it is on the owner. Translation: And if the value of the pawn is more, then on the mortgagee to the extent of the secured amount, and on the mortgagor to the extent of the excess, because the excess is an amanah in his hand, and the return is for restoring the hand, and his hand over the excess is the hand of the owner, for he is like a depositary over it, so for this reason (the ja'l for the excess) is on the owner. Explanation: If the slave's value is 200 rupees and the debt is 150 rupees, and the ja'l is e.g. 40 rupees, then 30 rupees are on the mortgagee and 10 on the mortgagor... A response to an objection: And this is contrary to the rent of the house that we mentioned, for all of it is obligatory on the mortgagee even if there is excess in the pawn's value.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case: when a mortgaged slave (rahn) runs away, who bears the cost (ja'l, i.e., the reward or wage) paid to the person who returns him? The ruling follows the general principle of protective expenses. Bringing back the slave is considered a protective act (hifazat), so the ja'l is on the mortgagee (murtaheen) by default. However, a detailed condition is introduced: the full ja'l is only on the mortgagee when the value of the slave equals the debt. If the slave's value exceeds the debt, the mortgagee's liability is limited to the proportion of the debt amount (madhmun), and the mortgagor bears the rest for the excess (ziyadah), because the excess value is held by the mortgagee as a trust (amanah) – like a depository (wadi'). The text then provides an example: if the slave is worth 200 and the debt is 150, and the ja'l is 40, then 30 (proportionate to 150/200) is on the mortgagee, and 10 (proportionate to 50/200) is on the mortgagor. The passage concludes with a distinction from the earlier ruling on house rent, where the entire rent is on the mortgagee regardless of value, because rent is a periodic expense for protection, while ja'l is a one-time recovery cost.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): A reward or wage paid to someone who recovers a lost or runaway item, such as a slave.
آبق (abaq): A runaway slave.
مضمون (madhmun): The amount secured by the pawn, i.e., the debt.
امانت (amanah): Trust; in this context, the excess value of the pawn over the debt is considered a trust held by the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged slave worth 300 dirhams is held for a debt of 200 dirhams, and someone returns him for a reward (ja'l) of 50 dirhams, how much does the mortgagee pay?
A) 50 dirhams
B) 33.33 dirhams (in proportion to 200/300 = 2/3)
C) 25 dirhams
D) 0 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The ja'l for returning a runaway pawn is split between mortgagee and mortgagor in proportion to their respective interests in the pawn's value.

Apportionment of Reward for Recovering an Absconding Mortgaged Slave
Explains the ruling on ja‘l for an absconding slave and its apportionment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the reward (ja‘l) for recovering an absconding mortgaged slave and apportion it correctly based on the pledge value relative to the debt.

Core Idea
The reward for recovering an absconding mortgaged slave is apportioned according to the secured portion, unlike rent which is entirely on the mortgagee.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the expense of recovering an absconding slave that has been pledged as collateral. The author distinguishes between expenses arising from the right of lien (habs) and those arising from the need for security (daman). Understanding this distinction is key to correctly allocating costs in mortgage transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is paying a reward (ja‘l) to someone who recovers an absconding mortgaged slave. The ruling: it is obligatory on the mortgagee (murtahin) when the value of the pledge equals the debt.
The obligation arises from the mortgagee's need to restore his right of possession (yad al-istifa).
2
Understand the rationale
The reward is part of the 'expense of return' (mu’nat al-radd). The mortgagee needs to recover the slave to secure the debt, so it is upon him initially. However, this is limited by the value of the debt.
The rationale is 'because he needs to restore the hand of istifa that he had' – a practical necessity.
3
Apply apportionment when value exceeds debt
If the pledge value is more than the debt, the reward is split: mortgagee pays proportion to the debt (madhmun), mortgagor pays the surplus portion. The surplus is held as a trust (amanah) for the owner.
The mortgagee is like a depositary (mudi‘) for the surplus; the owner must bear costs related to that surplus.
4
Contrast with the case of house rent
Rent for a house used for custody (habs) of the pledge is entirely on the mortgagee, even if the pledge value exceeds the debt. This is because rent arises from the right of lien (habs) which covers the whole property.
The reward is different: it arises from the need for security (daman), so it is apportioned according to the secured portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هذا القسم جعل الآبق فانه على المرتهن لانه محتاج الى اعادة يد الاستيفاء التي كانت له ليرده فكانت من مؤنة الرد فيلزمه وهذا اذا كانت قيمة الرهن والدين سواء. و ان كانت قيمة الرهن اكثر فعليه بقدر المضمون وعلى الراهن بقدر الزيادة عليه لانه امانة في يده والرد لاعادة اليد ويده في الزيادة يد المالك اذهو كالمودع فيها فلهذا يكون على المالك. و هذا بخلاف اجرة البيت الذي ذكرناه فإن كان كلها تجب على المرتهن وان كان في قيمة الرهن فضل لان وجوب ذلك بسبب الحبس وحق الحبس فى الكل ثابت له فاما الجعل انما يلزمه لاجل الضمان فيتقدر بقدر المضمون.
And from this category is the reward for the absconding slave: it is upon the mortgagee, because he needs to restore the hand of istifa that he had, in order to return him, so it is part of the expense of return and thus obligates him. And this is when the value of the pledge and the debt are equal. And if the value of the pledge is more, then upon him (the mortgagee) is to the extent of the secured portion, and upon the mortgagor is to the extent of the surplus over it, because it is a trust in his hand, and the return is for restoring the hand; and his hand in the surplus is the hand of the owner, for he is like a depositary in it, so for this reason it is upon the owner. And this is contrary to the rent of the house that we mentioned: indeed all of it is obligatory upon the mortgagee, even if there is a surplus in the value of the pledge, because its obligation is due to the lien, and the right of lien is established for him in the whole; as for the reward, it only obligates him because of the security, so it is apportioned according to the secured portion.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the reward (ja‘l) for recovering an absconding slave (abiq) that has been pledged as collateral (rahn). The author begins by categorizing this expense under the same principle as the previous rulings on maintenance. The reward is obligatory on the mortgagee (murtahin) because he needs to restore his right of possession (yad al-istifa) to secure the debt. However, this obligation applies fully only when the value of the pledged property equals the debt. If the value exceeds the debt, the reward is divided proportionally: the mortgagee bears the portion corresponding to the debt (the secured portion, madhmun), and the mortgagor (rahin) bears the portion corresponding to the surplus, because the surplus is held as a trust (amanah) on behalf of the owner. The passage then distinguishes this from the case of rent for a house that was previously discussed: the entire rent of a house used for custody is on the mortgagee because it arises from the right of lien (habs) which covers the whole property. The reward, however, arises from the need for security (daman), so it is limited to the amount of the debt. This distinction is crucial for understanding how different expenses on mortgaged property are apportioned.

Key Terms
جعل (ja‘l): Reward or compensation paid to someone who recovers an absconding slave.
آبق (abiq): A slave who has run away from his owner or mortgagee.
مرتہن (murtahin): The person holding the pledged property as security for a debt (mortgagee).
راہن (rahin): The person who pledges property as security (mortgagor).
مضمون (madhmun): The portion of the pledged property’s value that corresponds to the debt, for which the mortgagee is a secured creditor.
امانت (amanah): The surplus value of the pledge beyond the debt, held by the mortgagee as a trust for the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the value of the pledge is less than the debt.
B) When the value of the pledge equals the debt.
C) When the value of the pledge exceeds the debt.
D) Only if the mortgagee consents.

Key Takeaway
The reward for recovering an absconding mortgaged slave is apportioned proportionally to the debt and surplus, whereas rent for custody is entirely on the mortgagee.

Division of Medical & Diyat Expenses on a Mortgaged Slave
Ruling on division of expenses on mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for apportionment of medical and diyat expenses on a mortgaged slave and apply it to calculate each party's liability.

Core Idea
Expenses on a mortgaged slave are split between mortgagee and mortgagor in proportion to debt and surplus value.

The previous ruling established that the reward for returning a runaway slave is divided based on the secured and trust portions. This ruling extends the same principle to other expenses incurred on the slave, such as medical treatment and diyat. Understanding this division is crucial for correctly allocating financial responsibilities in a mortgage arrangement.

Guided Path
1
List the expenses covered
The ruling mentions treatment of wounds (jaraha), boils (qarha), illnesses (marad), and ransom for crimes (fida'). These are all costs that may arise from the slave.
2
Identify the two portions
The slave's total value is divided into two conceptual parts: madhmun (secured portion equal to the debt) and amanah (trust portion, the surplus value over the debt). The mortgagee holds the secured portion as collateral; the mortgagor retains ownership of the surplus.
If value ≤ debt, the entire slave is secured, so no trust portion exists.
3
Apply proportional division
Each expense is divided by the ratio of these two portions. For example, if debt is 150 and value is 200, the mortgagee's share is 150/200 = 3/4 of the expense, and the mortgagor's share is 50/200 = 1/4.
This proportion applies identically to every expense listed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و مداواة الجراحة ومعالجة القروح ومعالجة الامراض والفداء من الجناية ينقسم على المضمون والامانة.
And the treatment of wounds, and the curing of boils, and the treatment of illnesses, and the ransom from injury, are divided upon the secured portion and the trust.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This brief ruling extends the same principle of apportionment to other expenses incurred on a mortgaged slave. When the slave suffers a wound (jaraha), develops a boil (qarha), falls ill (marad), or commits a crime requiring ransom (fida'), the costs are divided proportionally between the mortgagee (murtahin) and the mortgagor (rahin) based on the ratio of debt and surplus value. This follows the logic established in the previous ruling on the reward (ja‘l): expenses necessitated by the security (daman) are on the mortgagee to the extent of the debt, while expenses related to the trust portion are on the owner. For example, if the slave is worth 200 and debt is 150, then 3/4 of the cost is on the mortgagee and 1/4 on the mortgagor.

Key Terms
مداواة (mudaawah): Treatment of wounds or injuries.
فداء (fida'): Ransom or compensation paid for a crime (jinayah) committed by the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only the mortgagor
C) Both proportionally
D) Neither; it is paid from the sale proceeds

Key Takeaway
Medical and diyat expenses on a mortgaged slave are divided proportionally between the mortgagee and mortgagor based on the debt and surplus value.

Kharaj on Mortgaged Property is the Mortgagor's Responsibility
States that kharaj is solely on the mortgagor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the land tax on a mortgaged property is solely the mortgagor's responsibility and explain the rationale based on expenses of ownership.

Core Idea
Ownership-based expenses like land tax stay with the owner, not the mortgagee.

This short but potent ruling settles the question of who bears the land tax (kharaj) on a mortgaged property. The answer is clear: the mortgagor (rahin) alone. The reason is that kharaj is an expense of ownership (mu'an al-mulk), and ownership remains with the mortgagor despite the property being pledged. This simple principle distinguishes ownership-based costs from other costs like maintenance or security.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the payment of kharaj (land tax) on a mortgaged property. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) on the mortgagor alone.
The ruling is stated declaratively: 'al-kharaj ala al-rahin khassah'.
2
Locate the rationale
The author gives the reason: 'because it is from the expenses of ownership (mu'an al-mulk)'. Understand that the tax is tied to ownership, not possession.
This rationalizes why the mortgagee is not liable: they only hold possession as security, not ownership.
3
Distinguish from other expenses
Not all expenses on the pledged property fall on the same party. For example, costs of maintenance or feeding an animal may be different. The key distinction is whether the expense arises from ownership or from possession/benefit.
In the fuller text, the author contrasts kharaj with other items like the reward for returning an absconding slave.
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
If a new tax or levy is introduced that is based on land ownership (e.g., property tax), it would follow the same rule: the mortgagor pays. This principle ensures consistency across similar scenarios.
The illah (effective cause) is the nature of the expense as mu'an al-mulk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخراج على الراهن خاصة لانه من مؤن الملك.
And the land tax is specifically upon the mortgagor because it is from the expenses of ownership.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This ruling addresses the land tax (kharaj) on agricultural land that has been pledged as security. Unlike other expenses such as the reward for returning an absconding slave or medical treatment, the land tax is entirely the responsibility of the mortgagor (rahin), not the mortgagee (murtahin). The reason given is that kharaj is an expense related to ownership (mulk), not to possession or security. The mortgagee merely holds the property as a security; ownership remains with the mortgagor. Therefore, any tax or levy that arises from the fact of ownership must be borne by the owner. This is a clear and simple rule with no apportionment.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land, paid to the state.
مؤن الملك (mu'an al-mulk): Expenses that arise from ownership, such as taxes and maintenance of the property's title.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagee.
B) The mortgagor.
C) Both equally.
D) The state directly.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is an ownership expense; therefore, it is solely the mortgagor's obligation.

Rent of the Mortgaged House Falls Entirely on the Mortgagee
Explaining the ruling on rent of the mortgaged house and the distinction between rent and guarantee payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the rent of a mortgaged house and explain the distinction between rent (ujrat) and guarantee payment (ju'l) regarding proportionality.

Core Idea
The entire rent of the mortgaged house is on the mortgagee because it stems from the right of retention, which is his exclusive benefit.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies a crucial distinction in mortgage rulings. The rent of a mortgaged property is not split proportionally like the guarantee payment (ju'l). Instead, the full rent is the responsibility of the mortgagee because it compensates for the benefit of holding the property (habd), which he enjoys entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: the entire rent of the mortgaged house is wajib on the mortgagee.
This applies even if the property value exceeds the debt.
2
Identify the cause (illa)
The obligation arises from the mortgagee's right of retention (habd) over the entire property. Since he holds the whole property, he owes compensation for the entire benefit of retention.
The right of retention is indivisible.
3
Compare with ju'l
The guarantee payment (ju'l) is measured proportionally to the debt because it compensates for the risk of guarantee, which is limited to the debt amount.
Ju'l is divisible according to the guaranteed amount.
4
Address the objection
Why not split rent proportionally? Because rent is for the benefit of retention, which is enjoyed entirely by the mortgagee, whereas ju'l is for the risk of loss, which is limited to the debt.
The cause (illa) differs, so the rulings differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لان وجوب ذلك بسبب الحبس وحق الحبس فى الكل ثابت له فاما الجعل انما يلزمه لاجل الضمان فيتقدر بقدر المضمون

ترجمہ اور یہ اس گھر کی اجرت کے خلاف ہے جس کو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں اس لئے کہ پوری اجرت مرتہن پر واجب ہوتی ہے اگر چہ رہن کی قیمت میں ( قرض سے ) زیادتی ہو اس لئے کہ اس کا (اجرت بیت کا ) وجوب جس کے سبب سے ہے اور جس کا حق مرتہن کے لئے کل میں ثابت ہے، بس بہر حال جعل مرتہن پر لازم ہوتا ہے عمان کے سبب سے تو جعل بقدر مضمون مقدر ہوگا۔

تشریح یہاں سے مصنف ایک اشکال کا جواب دینا چاہتے ہیں۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ جب رہن کی قیمت قرض سے زائد ہو تو بقدر دین کا جعل مرتہن کے ذمہ ہے اور زیادتی کا جعل راہن کے ذمہ ہے تو اسی طرح اگر رہن کی قیمت دین سے زیادہ ہو تو حفاظت کے کمرہ کا کرایہ مرتہن پر بقدر مضمون ہونا چاہیے اور زیادتی کا کرایہ راہن پر ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ آپ نے پوری اجرت مرتہن کے ذمہ لازم کر دی ہے؟ تو مصنف نے اس کا جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب مرتہن مرہون کو اپنے پاس روکتا ہے اور اس پر حفاظت جس کی وجہ سے ہے اور جس کل کا ہے لہذا پوری اجرت مرتہن پر واجب ہوگی اور مرتہن پر جعل کا لزوم جس کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ ضمان کی وجہ سے ہے اور مضمون بقدر دین ہے اور باقی امانت ہے۔ لہذا جو مقدار مضمون ہوگی اسی کا جعل مرتہن کے ذمہ ہو گا اور باقی کا جعل مالک ادا کرے گا۔
Because the obligation of that [rent] is due to retention, and the right of retention in the entirety is established for him. As for the guarantee payment (ju'l), it is only obligatory for him because of the guarantee, so it is measured according to the guaranteed amount. Translation: And this is contrary to the rent of this house which we have mentioned, because the entire rent is obligatory on the mortgagee even if the value of the mortgage exceeds the debt, because the obligation of rent is due to the cause [retention] and the right of retention is established for the mortgagee in its entirety. So, in any case, the guarantee payment is obligatory on the mortgagee due to the guarantee, so the guarantee payment is measured according to the guaranteed amount. Commentary: Here the author wants to answer an objection. The objection is: When the value of the mortgage exceeds the debt, the guarantee payment for the amount of debt is on the mortgagee, and the excess guarantee payment is on the mortgagor. So likewise, if the value of the mortgage exceeds the debt, the rent of the house for protection should be on the mortgagee to the extent of the guaranteed amount and the excess rent should be on the mortgagor, whereas you have made the entire rent obligatory on the mortgagee? So the author gives an answer: The mortgagee holds the mortgage with himself, and the protection is for him, and the entire rent is obligatory on the mortgagee. And the liability of guarantee payment (ju'l) on the mortgagee is not due to retention but due to guarantee, and the guaranteed amount is the amount of debt, and the rest is a trust. So whatever is the guaranteed amount, its guarantee payment is on the mortgagee, and the rest of the guarantee payment is paid by the owner.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the rent of a mortgaged property. The author begins by stating the reasoning for the ruling: the obligation of rent arises from the right of retention (habd), which belongs entirely to the mortgagee. Therefore, the full rent is on the mortgagee, even if the property value exceeds the debt. This is contrasted with the 'ju'l' (the payment for the guarantee of the debt), which is proportional to the guaranteed amount. The author then explains an objection: why shouldn't the rent be split proportionally like the ju'l? The answer is that the rent is compensation for the benefit of retention, which the mortgagee enjoys in full, while the ju'l is compensation for the risk of guarantee, which is limited to the debt amount. Thus, the rent is entirely on the mortgagee, while the ju'l is split proportionally between the mortgagee and the mortgagor.

Key Terms
جعل (ju'l): The payment owed by the mortgagor to the mortgagee as compensation for guaranteeing the debt, proportional to the debt amount.
اجرت (ujrat): Rent or hire payment for the house, which in the context of mortgage is completely on the mortgagee.
حبس (habd): Retention or withholding of the mortgaged property by the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the rent compensates for the right of retention (habd), which is indivisible
C) Because the guarantee payment (ju'l) is proportional, so rent must be proportional too
D) Because the mortgagor is not using the property

Key Takeaway
The entire rent of a mortgaged house is wajib on the mortgagee because it compensates for the indivisible benefit of retention, distinct from the proportional guarantee payment (ju'l).

Dividing Medical and Compensation Costs for a Mortgaged Slave
Explaining that expenses for medical treatment and diyah are divided between mortgagee and mortgagor proportionally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state how treatment and diyah costs for a mortgaged slave are divided between mortgagee and mortgagor and apply the proportional division method to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Expenses for a mortgaged slave are split proportionally between mortgagee and mortgagor based on the ratio of debt to value.

In this passage, the author explains a key principle in Hanafi mortgage law (rahn): when a mortgaged slave requires medical treatment or diyah for an injury, the cost is not borne entirely by one party. Instead, it is divided between the mortgagee (creditor) and the mortgagor (debtor) in proportion to the guaranteed portion (madhmun) and the trust portion (amanah) of the slave's value. This ensures equitable sharing of expenses according to each party's interest in the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two portions
Determine the slave's total value and the amount of debt. The guaranteed portion (madhmun) equals the debt; the trust portion (amanah) is the excess value.
2
Calculate the ratio
Compute the fraction of the value that is guaranteed: debt ÷ total value. This fraction represents the mortgagee's share of any expense.
Ensure the debt does not exceed the value; if it does, the entire value is guaranteed (amanah becomes zero).
3
Apply ratio to expenses
Multiply the total expense by the guaranteed fraction to find the mortgagee's liability. The remaining amount is the mortgagor's liability.
4
Verify with example
Check the example: slave worth 200 dirhams, debt 150 dirhams, expense 20 dirhams. Guaranteed fraction = 150/200 = 3/4. Mortgagee pays 3/4 × 20 = 15 dirhams; mortgagor pays 5 dirhams.
The same principle applies to any expense, not just treatment or diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و مداواة الجراحة ومعالجة القروح ومعالجة الامراض والفداء من الجناية ينقسم على المضمون والامانة

زخم کا علاج اور پھنسی پھوڑے کا علاج اور امراض کا علاج اور جنائیت کا فدیہ مضمون اور امانت پر تقسیم ہوگا

ترجمہ اور زخم کا علاج اور پھوڑے پھنسی کا علاج اور امراض کا علاج اور جنایت، ( مجرمانہ حرکت ) کا فدیہ مضمون اور امانت پر منقسم ہو گا۔ تشریح اگر غلام مرہون کو زخم ہو جائے یا اس کے پھوڑے پھنسی نکل آئیں یا دیگر امراض لاحق ہوجائیں یا کوئی ایسی مجرمانہ حرکت کر دے جس کا فدیہ ادا کرنا پڑے تو اس کا حساب حسب سابق ہوگا یعنی مضمون کی مقدار کا علاج و فدیہ مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگا اور امانت کی مقدار کارا ہن کے ذمہ ہو گا مثلاً غلام مرہون کی قیمت دو سو روپے ہے اور قرض ہے ایک سو پچاس روپے اور مذکورہ اشیاء میں شالا میں روپے خرچ ہوئے تو پندرہ مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوں گے اور پانچ راہن کے۔
And treating wounds, treating abscesses, treating diseases, and the ransom from injury/offence are divided between the guaranteed portion and the trust portion. Treatment of wounds and treatment of boils and treatment of diseases and compensation for criminal act will be divided on the guaranteed and trust. Translation and the treatment of wounds and treatment of boils and treatment of diseases and the diyah for criminal act is divided on the guaranteed and trust. Commentary: If the mortgaged slave gets wounded or has boils or other diseases or someone commits a criminal act for which diyah must be paid, then its account will be as before: the treatment and diyah for the guaranteed amount is on the mortgagee, and for the trust amount is on the mortgagor. For example, the value of the mortgaged slave is two hundred rupees and the debt is one hundred fifty rupees, and the mentioned expenses total twenty rupees, then fifteen will be on the mortgagee and five on the mortgagor.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on expenses for medical treatment and diyah (compensation for injuries) related to a mortgaged slave. The author states that these expenses are divided proportionally between the mortgagee and the mortgagor based on the portion of the slave's value that is guaranteed (the debt) and the portion that is a trust (the excess over the debt). The author gives a clear example: a slave worth 200 rupees is mortgaged for a debt of 150 rupees. Expenses of 20 rupees are incurred. The mortgagee bears 15 rupees (proportionate to the guaranteed 150/200 = 3/4 of 20) and the mortgagor bears 5 rupees (the remaining 1/4). This division follows the same principle as the earlier discussion on 'ju'l' (guarantee payment).

Key Terms
مضمون (madhmun): The portion of the mortgaged property's value that equals the debt, i.e., the guaranteed part.
امانة (amanah): The portion of the mortgaged property's value that exceeds the debt, considered a trust.
دية (diyah): Compensation paid for bodily injury or homicide.
رهن (rahn): Mortgage or pledge of property as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged slave worth 200 rupees is pledged for a debt of 150 rupees and treatment costs 20 rupees, how much does the mortgagee pay?
A) 20 rupees
B) 15 rupees
C) 5 rupees
D) 0 rupees

Key Takeaway
The cost of medical treatment and diyah for a mortgaged slave is divided between the mortgagee and mortgagor in proportion to their respective interests (debt and equity) in the slave.

Kharaj on Mortgaged Land: The Mortgagor Bears the Tax
Ruling statement with causal explanation (ta'lil).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who pays kharaj on mortgaged land and explain the underlying principle that kharaj follows ownership.

Core Idea
Kharaj follows ownership, not possession: the mortgagor alone must pay.

This short passage from Hidayah addresses a practical question in mortgage (rahn) transactions: when land subject to kharaj (land tax) is mortgaged, who is liable to pay the annual tax? The text gives a clear ruling based on a core Hanafi principle — that kharaj is a burden on ownership, and since the mortgagor remains the owner, he alone bears the tax. The mortgagee, despite holding possession, is not liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text explicitly states that kharaj is on the mortgagor specifically. This is the ruling to be applied.
The phrase 'والخراج على الراهن خاصة' ('and kharaj is on the mortgagor specifically') is the operative legal statement.
2
Locate the Causal Rationale (Ta'lil)
The author provides a reason: 'لانه من مؤن الملك' ('because it is from the burdens of ownership'). Identify this as the cause (illa) linking the ruling to the ownership status.
The Arabic word 'مؤن' (burdens) indicates expenses that naturally arise from owning property.
3
Understand the Ownership Principle
Recognize that in Hanafi law, kharaj is attached to the land itself and is a recurrent expense on whomever has the full right of disposal (milk). The mortgagor retains ownership, so he must bear this cost.
The mortgagee only has a possessory right as security, not ownership. This distinction is critical.
4
Apply to a Concrete Scenario
If a person mortgages his kharaji land to a creditor, the creditor (mortgagee) cannot be required to pay kharaj, even though he holds the land. The mortgagor remains liable each year.
This ruling ensures that the mortgagee's position is not unduly burdened, preserving the nature of rahn as a security contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخراج على الراهن خاصة لانه من مؤن الملك

خراج کس پر ہے

ترجمہ اور خراج خاص طور پر راہن کے ذمہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ خراج تو ملکیت کا بار ہے۔ تشریح اگر خراجی زمین رہن رکھی تو اس کا خراج کون ادا کرے گا تو فرمایا کہ راہن ادا کرے گا کیونکہ زمین کا مالک فقط راہن ہے اور خراج ملکیت کا بار اور خرچہ ہے لہذا وہ صرف راہن پر ہوگا۔
And kharaj is on the mortgagor specifically because it is from the burdens of ownership. On whom is kharaj? Translation: And kharaj is specifically on the mortgagor because kharaj is a burden of ownership. Commentary: If kharaji land is mortgaged, then who will pay its kharaj? He said that the mortgagor will pay it because the owner of the land is only the mortgagor, and kharaj is a burden and expense of ownership, so it will be only on the mortgagor.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage gives a brief ruling on kharaj (land tax) for mortgaged land. The author states that kharaj is on the mortgagor alone, because it is a cost that arises from ownership (milk). Since the mortgagor remains the legal owner during the mortgage, he bears the tax. The mortgagee only has a right to hold the property as security, not ownership, so he is not liable for ownership-related expenses like kharaj.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax levied on agricultural land, considered a burden on the owner.
مؤن الملك (mu'an al-milk): Burdens of ownership; expenses naturally arising from owning property, such as taxes and maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The state

Key Takeaway
Kharaj on mortgaged land is wajib solely on the mortgagor because it is a burden of ownership, not possession.
