Ushr from Produce Takes Priority Over Mortgagee's Right
Explaining that ushr from produce is taken before the mortgagee's security interest, and why this does not invalidate the mortgage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ushr is deducted before the mortgagee's right and distinguish why this does not invalidate the mortgage, contrasting with the case of istihqaq.

Core Idea
Ushr is attached to the substance, so it takes priority; mortgage remains valid because ownership is not divided.

In Hanafi law, when land subject to a mortgage produces crops, a question arises: does the mortgagee's security interest cover the full produce, or is a portion owed as ushr (the religious tithe on agricultural land) taken out first? This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the rule: ushr is given precedence over the mortgagee's right. The reasoning hinges on the nature of the two rights—one attached to the physical land (ayn), the other to its value. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of mortgage and tithe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Core Distinction
Read the ruling: ushr is taken first from the produce before the mortgagee's right. Note the reason given: 'li ta'alluqihi bil-'ayn' (because it is attached to the substance). Contrast this with the mortgagee's right, which is attached to the value.
This is a rational (aqli) proof.
2
Understand Why the Mortgage Remains Valid
The text states that the obligation of ushr does not negate the mortgagor's ownership. Since the mortgage is based on ownership, it remains valid on the remainder after ushr is paid. Recognize that ushr is a duty on the produce, not a division of the land itself.
The key is that ushr is a charge on the produce, not on the land's title.
3
Contrast with the Case of Istihqaq (Ownership Claim)
The author presents a counter-example: if someone proves a 1/10 share in the land, the mortgage becomes invalid because the land becomes musha' (shared). This violates the condition that the mortgaged item must be known and non-shared.
Istihqaq results in actual division of ownership, invalidating the mortgage.
4
Resolve the Apparent Contradiction
The text anticipates an objection: why does taking ushr (also 1/10 of produce) not make the land musha'? The answer lies in the flexibility: the owner can pay ushr from other grain, so the produce from the land itself is not necessarily divided. The land ownership remains intact and undivided.
Thus, ushr does not create a share in the land; it is merely an obligation that can be fulfilled from other sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعشر فيما يخرج مقدم على حق المرتهن لتعلقه بالعين ولا يبطل الرهن في الباقي لان وجوبه لا ينافي ملكه بخلاف الاستحقاق

عشر راہن پر ہے یا مرتہن پر

ترجمہ اور عشر پیداوار کا مرتین کے حق پر مقدم ہے عشر کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے عین کے ساتھ اور باقی میں رہن باطل نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ رہن کا وجوب ملک راہن کے منافی نہیں ہے بخلاف استحقاق کے۔ تشریح جو باغ یا درخت مرہون ہیں اگر ان کے اوپر پھل آئیں گے تو وہ راہن کی ملکیت ہوگی لیکن ان کو مرتہن کے پاس محبوس رکھا جائیگا جب راہن قرض ادا کر دے تو سب واپس لے لیگا۔ نیز ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ مشاع نہ ہو ور نہ عقدر من صحیح نہ ہو گا جب یہ بات ذہن نشین ہو گئی تو اب یہاں دو مسئلے ہیں۔

اگر زمین مرہون عشری ہے تو پیداوار کا عشر اولا نکالا جائے گا اور باقی نو حصوں کو مرتہن کے پاس رکھا جائے گا اور عشر کا نکالنا مرتہن کے حق سے مقدم ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ عشر کا تعلق مین رہن سے اور حق مرتین کا تعلق مالیت رہن سے اور جو حق عین سے مقدم ہو وہ اس حق سے مقدم ہوتا ہے جو مالیت سے ہو۔

۲۔ اگر کسی نے کوئی زمین رہن رکھی اور پھر کسی نے اس زمین کے ۱۰/ میں استحقاق کا دعوی کیا اور اپنے دعوے کو ثابت کر دیا تو رہن باطل ہو گیا کیونکہ مستحق کا عشر ۱۰را بطریق شیوع ہے حالانکہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ رہن کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ مشاع نہ ہو بہر حال صورت مذکورہ میں رہن باطل ہو گیا۔

سوال لہذا جب پیداوار کا عشر نکالا جائے گا تو یہ بھی بطریق شیوع ہے لہذا یہاں بھی رہن باطل ہو جانا چاہیے؟ جواب استحقاق کی صورت میں اسی زمین کا دسواں حصہ دینا ہوگا اور عشر کی صورت میں مالک کو اختیار ہے کہ اسی پیدا واز کا دسواں حصہ دیدے یا بقدر عشر اپنے پاس سے اس کے علاوہ غلہ دیدے لہذا اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ استحقاق کی صورت میں ملک راہن میں خلل واقع ہو گیا اور وہ مشاع ہو گئی اس لئے رہن باطل ہو گیا اور عنتر کی صورت میں راہن کی ملک میں کوئی خلل واقع نہیں ہوا اور پیداوار مشاع نہ ہوئی اس لئے یہاں رہن باطل نہ ہوگا۔
And the tithe (ushr) from what comes out (produce) is given precedence over the right of the mortgagee because of its attachment to the substance (ayn), and the mortgage is not invalidated in the remainder because its obligation does not negate his ownership, contrary to the case of claim (istiqaq). Is ushr on the mortgagor or mortgagee? Translation: And the ushr of produce is given precedence over the mortgagee's right because ushr is attached to the substance (ayn), and the mortgage is not invalidated in the remainder because the obligation of ushr does not conflict with the mortgagor's ownership, unlike the case of claim (istiqaq). Commentary: The fruits grown on mortgaged trees belong to the mortgagor, but they will be held by the mortgagee until the debt is paid. It has also preceded that it is necessary for the mortgaged item not to be musha' (shared); otherwise the mortgage contract is not valid. Keeping this in mind, there are two issues here: 1) If the land mortgaged is 'ushri land, the ushr is taken first from the produce, and the remaining nine-tenths are held by the mortgagee. Why is taking ushr given precedence over the mortgagee's right? Because ushr is attached to the substance (ayn) and the mortgagee's right is attached to the value; the right attached to the substance takes precedence over the right attached to the value. 2) If someone mortgages land and then someone claims ownership of a tenth of that land and proves it, the mortgage becomes invalid because the claimant's right is a specific share, making the land musha', whereas it is a condition that the mortgage not be musha'. So the mortgage is invalid. Question: When the ushr of produce is taken, that is also by way of sharing (shuyu'), so why doesn't the mortgage become invalid? Answer: In the case of claim (istiqaq), exactly one tenth of the land itself must be given, while in the case of ushr, the owner has the option to give one tenth of the produce or to give an equivalent amount of grain from elsewhere. Thus, in the case of claim, the mortgagor's ownership is affected and becomes shared, so the mortgage is invalid. In the case of ushr, the mortgagor's ownership is not affected and the produce is not considered shared, so the mortgage is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage deals with the interaction between ushr (the tithe on agricultural produce) and the rights of the mortgagee. The author first states the ruling: the ushr from the produce of mortgaged land is given priority over the mortgagee's right because ushr is a right attached to the land itself (bil-'ayn), while the mortgagee's right is attached to the value. Therefore, the ushr is deducted first, and the remainder is held as security. The mortgage remains valid on the remainder because paying ushr does not conflict with the mortgagor's ownership—it is an obligation on the produce, not the land's ownership structure. The author then contrasts this with a case of istihqaq (claim of ownership): if someone successfully claims a 1/10 share of the land, the mortgage becomes invalid because the land becomes musha' (shared), which violates the condition that the mortgaged item be non-shared. The author answers a potential objection: why does paying ushr (which also involves taking 1/10 of produce) not make the land musha'? The key difference is that in ushr, the owner has the option to pay the equivalent value from other grain, so the land itself remains fully owned by the mortgagor without division. Thus, the mortgage remains valid.

Key Terms
عشر (ushr): The tithe (10%) levied on agricultural produce from 'ushri land (land owned by Muslims).
استحقاق (istiqaq): A legal claim of ownership, often by inheritance or purchase, which if proven can invalidate a mortgage because it divides the property.
مشاع (musha'): Undivided share or co-ownership; a mortgaged item must not be musha'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the owner can pay ushr from other grain, avoiding division of the actual land
C) Because the mortgagee agrees to it
D) Because the land is not musha' anyway

Key Takeaway
Ushr is taken from produce before the mortgagee's right because it is attached to the substance, and the mortgage remains valid since ownership is not divided.

Voluntary Payment by One Party Without Qadi's Order is Not Reimbursable
Explaining the rule on reimbursement when one party pays an obligation of the other in a mortgage contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on reimbursement when one party pays another's obligation in a mortgage and distinguish between voluntary payment and payment ordered by a qadi.

Core Idea
Without a qadi's order, paying another's debt is voluntary and non-reimbursable.

In a mortgage (rahn), certain expenses like rent or maintenance fall on specific parties. Sometimes one party pays an expense that was the other's responsibility. This lesson examines when such payment can be recovered. The key distinction is whether the payment was made voluntarily or by order of the qadi (judge).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their obligations
In a mortgage, the mortgagor (raahin) and mortgagee (murtahin) each have specific obligations. For example, the mortgagee is usually responsible for the property's rent, while the mortgagor is responsible for maintenance (nafaqah).
Know which party owes what in a standard mortgage.
2
Distinguish the two payment scenarios
The passage presents two situations: (1) One party pays the other's obligation without any order; (2) One party pays by order of the qadi. The ruling on reimbursement differs in each case.
3
Identify the ruling for voluntary payment
If a party voluntarily pays the other's obligation without a qadi's order, the payer is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi'). He cannot reclaim the amount from the other party.
Voluntary payment is akin to a gift; no reimbursement.
4
Identify the ruling for payment by qadi's order
If the qadi orders a party to pay the other's obligation, the payer can reclaim the amount from the original obligor. This is because the qadi's authority (wilayat al-qadi) is general and binds the obligor.
The qadi's order creates a legal obligation for the other party to repay.
5
Understand the rationale
The rationale for the distinction is that a voluntary payment lacks a legal basis for recourse, whereas a qadi's order provides a binding authority that makes reimbursement wajib on the original obligor.
The principle: 'al-wilayah al-ammah' (general authority) justifies enforcement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما اداه احدهما مما وجب على صاحبه فهو متطوع وما انفق احدهما مما يجب على الآخر بامر القاضي رجع عليه كان صاحبه امره به لان ولاية القاضي عامة

راہن نے مرتہن یا مرتہن نے راہن کی طرف سے کوئی چیز ادا کر دی تو یہ متطوع ہے

ترجمہ اور جوادا کر دیا ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے اس خرچہ میں سے جو اس کے ساتھی پر واجب تھا تو وہ متطوع ہے اور جو خرچ کیا ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے اس خرچہ میں سے جو دوسرے پر واجب تھا قاضی کے حکم سے تو وہ اس پر رجوع کرے گا کہ اس کے ساتھی نے اس کو اس کا حکم کیا ہے اس لئے کہ قاضی کی ولایت عام ہے۔ تشریح حفاظت رہن کے گھر کا کرایہ مرتہن کے ذمہ تھا لیکن ادا کر دیا راہن نے اسی طرح نفقہ را بہن کے ذمہ واجب تھا لیکن ادا کر دیا
And whatever one of them pays from what was obligatory on his companion, he is a volunteer. And whatever one of them spends from what is obligatory on the other by the order of the qadi, he will have recourse against him, as if his companion had ordered him to do it, because the authority of the qadi is general. If the mortgagor pays or the mortgagee pays something on behalf of the other, he is a volunteer. Translation: And whatever one of them pays from the expenses that were obligatory on his companion, he is a volunteer. And whatever one of them spends from what is obligatory on the other by the order of the qadi, he will have recourse against him, as if his companion had ordered him, because the qadi's authority is general. Commentary: The rent of the house for protection was on the mortgagee, but the mortgagor paid it; similarly, the maintenance (nafaqa) was obligatory on the mortgagor, but the mortgagee paid it...
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides a rule about reimbursement when one party to a mortgage pays an expense that was legally the other's responsibility. The author distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If someone pays an obligation of the other voluntarily without a court order, he is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi') and cannot claim reimbursement; it is like a gift. (2) If he pays by order of the qadi (judge), he can reclaim the amount from the other party, because the qadi's authority to order such payments is general and binding. The commentary gives examples: the mortgagor paid the house rent (which was on the mortgagee), or the mortgagee paid the maintenance (nafaqa) of the slave (which was on the mortgagor).

Key Terms
متطوع (mutatawwi'): A volunteer who performs an act without expectation of compensation; in this context, paying another's obligation voluntarily.
ولایة القاضی (wilayat al-qadi): The general authority of the qadi to order the fulfillment of obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, he is considered a volunteer
C) Only if the mortgagee agreed
D) Only if the amount is small

Key Takeaway
Without a qadi's order, paying another's obligation in a mortgage is deemed voluntary and non-reimbursable.

Priority of 'Ushr Over the Mortgagee's Right
Ruling with proof on precedence of 'ushr over mortgagee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the precedence of 'ushr over the mortgagee's right and distinguish it from the case of istihqaq.

Core Idea
The right attached to the 'ayn ('ushr) prevails over the right attached to value (mortgagee's claim).

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: when a mortgaged 'ushri land produces crops, the tithe ('ushr) must be taken first, before the mortgagee's right to hold the produce as security. The mortgage remains valid on the remaining produce. We will explore the reasoning and contrast it with the case of a third-party ownership claim (istihqaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing claims
Recognize that the obligation of 'ushr on the produce and the mortgagee's right to hold the produce as security are both valid claims against the produce.
2
Analyze the nature of each right
Understand that 'ushr is attached to the physical 'ayn (the produce itself), while the mortgagee's right is attached to the value (maliyyah) of the property.
The text states 'لتعلقه بالعين' for 'ushr.
3
Apply the precedence principle
Apply the rule that a right attached to the 'ayn takes precedence over a right attached to value; thus 'ushr is taken first.
This is the core argument (dalil aqli/istihsan).
4
Check effect on the mortgage
Since the obligation of 'ushr does not negate the mortgagor's ownership of the land, the mortgage remains valid on the remaining nine-tenths of the produce.
Contrast with istihqaq where ownership is disturbed.
5
Distinguish from istihqaq
In istihqaq, a specific share of the land itself is claimed, making the land undivided (musha'), which invalidates the mortgage. In 'ushr, the owner can pay from other grain, so the land remains unaffected.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

خراج ملکیت کا بار اور خرچہ ہے لہذا وہ صرف راہن پر ہوگا۔
عشر راہن پر ہے یا مرتہن پر
والعشر فيما يخرج مقدم على حق المرتهن لتعلقه بالعين ولا يبطل الرهن في الباقي لان وجوبه لا ينافي ملكه بخلاف الاستحقاق
ترجمہ اور عشر پیداوار کا مرتین کے حق پر مقدم ہے عشر کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے عین کے ساتھ اور باقی میں رہن باطل نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ رہن کا وجوب ملک راہن کے منافی نہیں ہے بخلاف استحقاق کے۔ تشریح جو باغ یا درخت مرہون ہیں اگر ان کے اوپر پھل آئیں گے تو وہ راہن کی ملکیت ہوگی لیکن ان کو مرتہن کے پاس محبوس رکھا جائیگا جب راہن قرض ادا کر دے تو سب واپس لے لیگا۔ نیز ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ مشاع نہ ہو ور نہ عقدر من صحیح نہ ہو گا جب یہ بات ذہن نشین ہو گئی تو اب یہاں دو مسئلے ہیں۔
اگر زمین مرہون عشری ہے تو پیداوار کا عشر اولا نکالا جائے گا اور باقی نو حصوں کو مرتہن کے پاس رکھا جائے گا اور عشر کا نکالنا مرتہن کے حق سے مقدم ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ عشر کا تعلق مین رہن سے اور حق مرتین کا تعلق مالیت رہن سے اور جو حق عین سے مقدم ہو وہ اس حق سے مقدم ہوتا ہے جو مالیت سے ہو۔
۲۔ اگر کسی نے کوئی زمین رہن رکھی اور پھر کسی نے اس زمین کے ۱۰/ میں استحقاق کا دعوی کیا اور اپنے دعوے کو ثابت کر دیا تو رہن باطل ہو گیا کیونکہ مستحق کا عشر ۱۰را بطریق شیوع ہے حالانکہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ رہن کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ مشاع نہ ہو بہر حال صورت مذکورہ میں رہن باطل ہو گیا۔

Book of Mortgage. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 14. The kharaj (land tax) is a burden on ownership and expense, so it will be only on the mortgagor. Is the tithe on the mortgagor or mortgagee? And the tithe on what is produced is given precedence over the right of the mortgagee because of its attachment to the 'ayn, and the mortgage is not invalidated in the remainder because its obligation does not contradict his ownership, unlike a claim of ownership. Translation: The tithe of the produce is given precedence over the right of the mortgagee due to its attachment to the 'ayn, and the mortgage will not be invalidated for the remainder because the obligation of the mortgage does not contradict the ownership of the mortgagor, unlike a claim of ownership. Explanation: If a garden or trees are mortgaged and they produce fruit, the fruit belongs to the mortgagor but will be kept in the possession of the mortgagee. When the mortgagor repays the debt, he will take everything back. Also, it has passed earlier that for the mortgaged property it is necessary that it not be undivided (musha'), otherwise the contract would not be valid. Now that this is understood, there are two issues here. 1. If the mortgaged land is 'ushri (subject to tithe), then the tithe will be taken first from the produce, and the remaining nine parts will be kept with the mortgagee. Taking the tithe is given precedence over the right of the mortgagee. Why? Because the tithe is attached to the 'ayn of the mortgage, and the right of the mortgagee is attached to the value (maliyyah) of the mortgage. And a right that is attached to the 'ayn takes precedence over a right attached to the value. 2. If someone mortgaged a piece of land, and then someone claimed a right of ownership (istihqaq) in one-tenth of that land and proved his claim, then the mortgage becomes invalid because the claimant's one-tenth is by way of shuyu' (undivided share), whereas it has passed earlier that it is necessary for the mortgage that it not be undivided. In any case, in the mentioned scenario, the mortgage becomes invalid. Question: When the tithe on produce is taken, that also is by way of shuyu', so here too the mortgage should become invalid? Answer: In the case of istihqaq, the specific one-tenth of the land must be given, while in the case of tithe, the owner has the option to give one-tenth of that produce or give grain equivalent to the tithe from elsewhere. Therefore, from this detail it is understood that in the case of istihqaq, the ownership of the mortgagor is disturbed and it becomes undivided, so the mortgage is invalid; in the case of tithe, no disturbance occurs in the ownership of the mortgagor and the produce does not become undivided, so the mortgage is not invalid.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the interaction between 'ushr (tithe on agricultural produce) and the rights of a mortgagee (murtahin) when the mortgaged property is 'ushri land. The ruling is that the tithe on the produce is taken first, ahead of the mortgagee's right to hold the produce as security. The reasoning is that the tithe is attached to the physical 'ayn (the produce itself), whereas the mortgagee's right is attached only to the value (maliyyah) of the property. Rights attached to the 'ayn take precedence over rights attached to value. The mortgage remains valid on the remaining nine-tenths of the produce because the obligation of tithe does not contradict the mortgagor's ownership. The passage then contrasts this with a case of istihqaq (a third party establishing ownership of a share of the land). In that case, the mortgage becomes invalid because the property becomes undivided (musha'), which is a condition for a valid mortgage. The author resolves a potential objection: why doesn't 'ushr cause the same undividedness and invalidate the mortgage? The answer is that in istihqaq, the specific share is taken from the land itself, causing shuyu' in the land, whereas in 'ushr, the owner can pay the tithe from the produce or from elsewhere, so the land itself remains unaffected.

Key Terms
عشر (‘ushr): The tithe or one-tenth tax on agricultural produce from 'ushri (non-kharaj) land, which is an obligatory payment.
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee or pledgee who holds the mortgaged property as security for a debt.
راہن (rāhin): The mortgagor or pledgor who gives the property as security.
مشاع (mushā‘): Undivided share or common ownership; a condition for a valid mortgage is that the property be fully owned and not subject to undivided shares (except in certain cases).
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A claim of ownership by a third party that is proven, resulting in the property being partly owned by another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the mortgage remain valid when 'ushr is taken from the produce, but become invalid when a third party proves ownership (istihqaq) of a share of the land?
A) Because 'ushr is attached to the value while istihqaq is attached to the 'ayn.
B) Because in 'ushr the owner can pay from other grain, so the land is not divided; in istihqaq the specific share must be taken from the land, making it musha'.
C) Because 'ushr is a religious obligation while istihqaq is a legal claim.
D) Because the mortgagee's consent is required for 'ushr but not for istihqaq.

Key Takeaway
The tithe ('ushr) on produce takes precedence over the mortgagee's right because it attaches to the physical produce ('ayn), while the mortgagee's right attaches to value, and the mortgage remains valid as the owner can pay the tithe from elsewhere.

Recovery of Expenses in Mortgage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the ruling on recovery of expenses, then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute from Nawadir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on recovery of expenses paid for another in a mortgage, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in the Nawadir transmission regarding the effect of the other party's presence.

Core Idea
Without a qadi's order, payment is voluntary; with it, recovery is allowed—but Abu Hanifa denies recovery if the other party is present, due to limits on the qadi's authority.

This lesson examines a key question in mortgage (rahn): if one party pays an expense that was due on the other, can he recover it? The general rule is clear, but a dispute within the Hanafi school—transmitted in the Nawadir—reveals a deeper principle about the qadi's power to impose interdiction (hajr). Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how wilaya 'amma functions in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general rule
The act is one party paying an expense that is legally due on the other party in a mortgage (e.g., rent or maintenance). The general rule from Zahir al-Riwayah: if the payment is made without a qadi's order, the payer is a volunteer (mutatawwi‘) and cannot recover; if made by order of the qadi, recovery is allowed because the qadi's general authority (wilaya ‘amma) makes it as if the other party ordered the payment.
The distinction hinges on the qadi's order transforming the act from voluntary to agency.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute in Nawadir
In the Nawadir (rare transmissions), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on a specific scenario: if the other party is present (not absent), can the payer recover even with a qadi's order? Abu Hanifa says no; Abu Yusuf says yes, in both cases (present or absent).
Abu Hanifa's view is that the qadi cannot effectively place a present, capable adult under interdiction (hajr), so the order does not create valid agency.
3
Understand the underlying usul: hajr
The dispute is a branch of the issue of hajr. Abu Hanifa holds that a qadi cannot impose interdiction on a free, sane, adult who is present; thus the qadi's order is ineffective. Abu Yusuf holds that the qadi's general authority extends to present persons, so the order is valid.
This shows how a usul principle (limits of qadi's authority) directly shapes a fiqh ruling.
4
Compare the two positions and their thamarah
Practical consequence: If the other party is present and the qadi orders payment, according to Abu Hanifa the payer cannot recover; according to Abu Yusuf, he can. The Zahir al-Riwayah (general rule) does not mention presence, so recovery is generally allowed with a qadi's order.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the actual legal outcome in a real dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling: recovery is allowed when the qadi orders, regardless of presence. The Nawadir views are minority positions and not operative in fatwa.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah (strong); Nawadir (weak).

اقوال فقہاء
وعن ابي حنيفة ان لا يرجع اذا كان صاحبه حاضرًا وان كان بامر القاضى وقال ابو يوسف يرجع في الوجهين وهي فرع مسالة الحجر والله اعلم
ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ سے ( نوادر میں ) منقول ہے کہ وہ رجوع نہیں کرے گا جبکہ اس کا ساتھی موجود ہوا اگر چہ یہ قاضی کے حکم سے ہو اور ابو یوسف نے (نوادر میں ) فرمایا کہ دونوں صورتوں میں رجوع کرے گا اور یہ مسئلہ حجر کی فرع ہے واللہ اعلم
تشریح نوادر میں اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کا اختلاف نقل کیا گیا ہے جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر وہ دوسرا ساتھی جس طرف سے خرچ کیا گیا ہے غائب نہیں ہے بلکہ حاضر موجود ہے اور اس کی جانب سے دوسرے ساتھی نے اگروہ دوسرا ساتھی جس سے ہے نہیںہے نے خرچ کر دیا اگر چہ قاضی کے حکم سے خرچ کیا ہوا اپنے ساتھی سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔
اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ بہر صورت واپس لے سکتا ہے خواہ دوسرا ساتھی حاضر ہو یا غائب ہو خلاصہ کلام امام صاحب کے نزد یک رجوع جائز نہیں اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک رجوع جائز ہے اس پر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ حجر کے مسئلہ کی فرع ہے۔ سوال ... اس کا کیا مطلب ہے؟ جواب امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قاضی کو یہ ولایت نہیں ہے کہ وہ آزاد عاقل بالغ آدمی کو مجور قرار دے جو کہ حاضر و موجود ہے اور اگر قاضی نے حجر اس پر عائد کیا تو وہ غیر معتبر ہو گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی کو یہ ولایت ہے کہ وہ شخص مذکور کو مجور قرار دے۔ سوال یہ بات تو سمجھ میں آگئی لیکن فرعیت کا مسئلہ سمجھ میں نہیں آیا؟ جواب جب امام صاحب کے حاضر پر حجر جائز نہیں ہے تو اگر چہ قاضی نے اس کو اجازت دیدی کہ تو اس کی جانب سے خرچ کر دے حالانکہ وہ موجود و حاضر ہے غائب نہیں ہے تو گویا قاضی اس کو مجور قرار دے رہا ہے لیکن حجر غیر معتبر ہے اور وہ مجور نہیں ہوا جب وہ مجور نہیں ہوا تو خرچ کرنے والے کا خرچ تبرع اور تطوع ہوگا جس میں واپسی کا حق نہیں ہوا کرتا۔
اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جب قاضی نے دوسرے کو خرچ کرنے کی اجازت دیدی تو گویا اس کو مجور قرار دیا اور یہ حجر درست ہے جب حجر درست ہوا تو گویا خرچ کرنے والا اس کا ولی ہو گیا اور ولایت کا سبب امرقاضی ہے لہذا اس کو حق ہو گا کہ وہ اپنا حق اپنے ساتھی سے واپس لے لے۔
If the mortgagor paid something on behalf of the mortgagee, or the mortgagee on behalf of the mortgagor, then he is a volunteer. And what one of them paid from what was obligatory on his companion, he is a volunteer, and what one of them spent from what was obligatory on the other by order of the qadi, he may recover from him, as if his companion had ordered him to do so, because the authority of the qadi is general. Translation: And what one of them paid from the expense that was obligatory on his companion, then he is a volunteer. And what one of them spent from what was obligatory on the other by the order of the qadi, then he will recover from him, as if his companion had ordered him to do so, because the authority of the qadi is general. Explanation: The rent for the house where the mortgaged property was kept was due on the mortgagee, but the mortgagor paid it; similarly, maintenance (nafaqa) was due on the mortgagor, but the mortgagee paid it. Then they have the right to recover the amount spent from the other. It was said: if this spending was by the order of the qadi, then he can recover; if without the order of the qadi, then he cannot recover. The reason for not recovering is that the spender is a benefactor and volunteer, who does not have the right of recovery. And the reason for recovery is that when the qadi ordered him to do so, it is as if his companion himself had ordered him to spend, because the qadi has general authority, and in that case recovery is allowed. So here too recovery will be allowed. This entire detail is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. Statements of the jurists: And from Abu Hanifa (in Nawadir) that he will not recover when his companion is present, even if it was by order of the qadi. And Abu Yusuf said: he will recover in both cases. And this is a branch of the issue of hajr (interdiction). And Allah knows best. Translation: And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated (in Nawadir) that he will not recover when his companion is present, even if it was by order of the qadi. And Abu Yusuf said (in Nawadir) that he will recover in both cases. And this issue is a branch of the issue of hajr, and Allah knows best. Explanation: In Nawadir, the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf on this issue is narrated. The detail is that Imam Abu Hanifa says: if the other companion on whose behalf the expenditure was made is not absent but rather present and available, and the other companion spent on his behalf even by order of the qadi, he cannot recover from his companion. And Imam Abu Yusuf says: in any case he can recover, whether the other companion is present or absent. Summary: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, recovery is not allowed; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, recovery is allowed. On this, the author of Hidayah says: this is a branch of the issue of hajr. Question: What does that mean? Answer: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the qadi does not have the authority to place a free, sane, adult person under interdiction (hajr) who is present and available. If the qadi imposes hajr on him, it is invalid. And according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the qadi has the authority to place such a person under interdiction. Question: I understood that, but how is it a branch? Answer: Since Imam Abu Hanifa does not consider hajr valid on a present person, then even if the qadi gave permission for him to spend on his behalf while he is present and not absent, it is as if the qadi is placing him under interdiction, but that interdiction is invalid, so he is not placed under interdiction. When he is not under interdiction, the spending of the spender is a gift and voluntary, in which there is no right of recovery. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, when the qadi gave permission to the other to spend, it is as if he placed him under interdiction, and this interdiction is valid. When the interdiction is valid, then the spender becomes his guardian (wali), and the cause of guardianship is the order of the qadi. Therefore, he will have the right to recover his right from his companion.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where one party to a mortgage (either rahin or murtahin) pays an expense that is legally due on the other party. The general ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah is that if the payment is made without an order from the qadi, it is considered voluntary (tatawwu') and cannot be recovered. However, if the payment is made by order of the qadi, the payer can recover from the other party because the qadi's authority (wilaya 'amma) makes it as if the other party himself ordered the payment. The text then presents a notable intra-Hanafi dispute from the Nawadir (rare transmissions). According to Abu Hanifa, if the other party is present (i.e., not absent), then even if the payment was made by qadi's order, the payer cannot recover. According to Abu Yusuf, recovery is possible in both cases (whether the other party is present or absent). The commentator explains that this dispute is a branch of the issue of hajr (interdiction). Abu Hanifa holds that a qadi cannot place a free, sane, adult person under interdiction when that person is present and capable, so the qadi's order does not create a valid agency; thus, the payment remains voluntary. Abu Yusuf holds that the qadi does have such authority, so the order creates a valid guardianship, entitling the payer to recovery.

Key Terms
متطوع (mutaṭawwi‘): A volunteer who performs an act without legal obligation and without expectation of compensation.
رجوع (rujū‘): The right to recover or claim back money paid on behalf of another.
قاضی (qāḍī): A judge appointed by the state with general authority (wilaya 'amma) to adjudicate and enforce obligations.
ولایت (wilāyah): Legal authority or jurisdiction, here referring to the qadi's general authority over matters.
حجر (ḥajr): Interdiction or legal restriction placed on a person's financial rights, often due to incapacity or debt.
مجور (mujawwar): A person placed under interdiction (hajr) by the qadi, losing some financial autonomy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Nawadir transmission, what is the difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding recovery when one mortgage party pays an expense due on the other by order of the qadi, and the other party is present?
A) Abu Hanifa allows recovery; Abu Yusuf does not.
B) Abu Hanifa disallows recovery; Abu Yusuf allows recovery.
C) Both allow recovery if the other party is absent.
D) Both disallow recovery if the other party is present.

Key Takeaway
The general Hanafi rule allows recovery when payment is made by qadi's order; the Nawadir dispute shows that Imam Abu Hanifa's view ties recovery to the absence of the other party due to limitations on the qadi's power of hajr.

Pawning Undivided Property is Invalid: Two Hanafi Proofs
Inter-madhhab dispute with two Hanafi proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pawning an undivided share and explain the two proofs (yad al-istīfā' and habs dā'im) that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Pawning an undivided share fails because exclusive possession is impossible — continuous detention is the essence of rahn.

This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i on the validity of pawning an undivided share (mushā') in joint property. The Hanafi school rules it invalid, while the Shafi'i school permits it. The Hanafis provide two rational proofs to support their position, both centered on the requirement of exclusive physical control. Understanding these proofs will sharpen your ability to differentiate between contracts based on their legal effects.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i objection
Begin by identifying the clear ruling: pawning musha' is invalid. Note that al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding it valid. Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf (difference of opinion).
The matn from al-Quduri is the source of the Hanafi ruling.
2
Examine the first Hanafi proof: yad al-istīfā'
The first proof argues that the legal effect of a valid pawn is the establishment of a 'hand of recovery' – the murtahin's right to seize and hold the pawn to recover the debt. This requires that the pawn be under the exclusive physical control of the murtahin, which is impossible in an undivided share because the co-owner also has rights.
The Shafi'i position sees rahn merely as designation for sale, which does not require exclusive possession.
3
Examine the second Hanafi proof: habs dā'im
The second proof emphasizes that rahn requires continuous detention (habs dā'im) from the moment of contract until the debt is paid. In musha', time-sharing (muhāyāh) becomes necessary to allow the co-owner use of the property, breaking the continuity. This is analogous to a condition that the pawn alternate between parties, which is invalid even for divisible property.
The text explicitly compares this to saying 'I pawn to you for a day and not for a day' – which is clearly invalid.
4
Understand the Shafi'i counter-position and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i view is that the purpose of rahn is to designate the item for sale upon default. Since a musha' share can be sold, it can be pawned. The Hanafi response is implicit: the rahn contract has its own specific requirements (exclusive possession, continuous detention) that go beyond mere saleability. The textual basis 'farihanun maqbudatan' (the Quranic phrase) supports the possession requirement.
This distinction is crucial: each contract type has its own defining effect.
5
Distinguish rahn from hibah using the passage
The passage contrasts rahn with gift (hibah). In hibah, an undivided share in indivisible property is valid because the ruling of hibah is mere ownership (milk), which musha' can accept. The impediment in hibah is only the harm of forced division (gharāmah al-qismah), which does not apply if division is impossible. In rahn, the impediment is the inability to establish yad al-istīfā' and habs dā'im, which cannot be overcome even if the property is indivisible.
This comparison reinforces that the ruling is not about divisibility but about the nature of the contract's effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرهن
باب ما يجوز ارتهانه والارتهان به و ما لا يجوز
قال ولا يجوز رهن المشاع وقال الشافعي يجوز ولنا فيه وجهان احدها يبتنى على حكم الرهن فإنه عندنا ثبوت يد الاستيفاء ولهذا لا يتصور فيما يتناوله العقد وهو المشاع وعنده المشاع يقبل ما هو الحكم عنده وهو تعينه للبيع
والثاني ان موجب الرهن هو الحبس الدائم لانه لم يشرع الا مقبوضا بالنص أو بالنظر الى المقصود منه وهو الاستيثاق من الوجه الذي بيناه وكل ذلك يتعلق بالدوام ولا يفضى اليه الا استحقاق الحبس ولو جوزناه في المشاع يفوت الدوام لانه لا بد من المهاياة فبصير كما اذا قال رهنتك يوما ويوما لا ولهذا لا يجوز فيما يحتمل القسمة وما لا يحتملها
بخلاف الهبة حيث تجوز فيما لا يحتمل القسمة لان المانع فى الهبة غرامة القسمة وهو فيما يقسم اما حكم الهبة الملك والمشاع يقبله وههنا الحكم ثبوت يد الاستيفاء والمشاع لا يقبله وان كان لا يحتمل القسمة
Book of Rahn. Chapter on what is valid to pawn and what to pawn with, and what is not valid. He (al-Quduri) said: 'Pawning an undivided share (mushā') is not valid.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'It is valid.' For us there are two proofs. One is based on the ruling of rahn: for us it is the establishment of the hand of recovery (yad al-istīfā'), and therefore it is not conceivable in something that the contract encompasses, which is the undivided share. According to him, the undivided share accepts what is the ruling according to him, which is its designation for sale. The second proof is that the consequence of rahn is continuous detention (habs dā'im), because it is legislated only as possessed by text or by consideration of its purpose, which is securing (al-istīthāq) in the way we explained. All of this relates to continuity, and it is only achieved through the right of detention. If we permitted it in undivided property, continuity would be lost because time-sharing (muhāyāh) becomes necessary, so it becomes like when one says 'I pawn to you for a day and not for a day.' For this reason, it is not valid in that which can be divided or that which cannot be divided. Unlike hibah (gift), which is valid for what cannot be divided, because the impediment in hibah is the harm of division (gharāmat al-qismah), which applies to what can be divided. However, the ruling of hibah is ownership (milk), and the undivided share accepts it. Here in rahn, the ruling is the establishment of yad al-istīfā', and the undivided share does not accept it, even if it cannot be divided.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of pawning an undivided share (mushā') in joint property. The matn from al-Quduri states the Hanafi position: pawning musha' is not valid. Al-Shafi'i permits it. The commentator then presents two Hanafi proofs. The first is based on the nature of rahn: according to the Hanafis, the legal effect of a valid pawn is the establishment of a 'hand of recovery' (yad al-istīfā')—meaning the pawned item must remain in the exclusive custody of the pawnbroker (murtahin) until the debt is paid, so that he can recover his due from its value. This requires that the pawn be fully possessed by the murtahin. In a musha' share, exclusive possession is impossible because another party (the co-owner) also has rights. Therefore, the contract cannot achieve its intended effect. Al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, holds that the legal effect of rahn is simply to designate the pawn for sale in case of default—a mere legal designation that does not require physical exclusive possession. Since a musha' share can be sold, it can also be pawned. The second Hanafi proof is based on the requirement that the pawn remain continuously detained (habs da'im) with the murtahin. This continuity is essential because the Quran calls for a pawn 'in hand' (farihanun maqbudatan) and because the purpose of pawning is to secure the debt by preventing the pawner from denying the loan or disposing of the pawn. If musha' were allowed, the pawn would have to be shared via time-sharing (muhayāh), breaking the continuous detention. This would be like a condition that the pawn alternate between the murtahin and the pawner—which is invalid even in a divided property. Hence, musha' pawn is invalid whether or not it can be physically divided. The passage then contrasts with hibah (gift). In hibah, a gift of an undivided share is valid only if the property cannot be divided (e.g., a small share in a well) because the impediment is the harm of forced division, which does not apply if division is impossible. Moreover, the ruling of hibah is mere ownership (milk), which is possible in undivided shares. In rahn, however, the ruling is yad al-istīfā', which musha' does not accept. Thus, the distinction is based on the different legal effects. The Hanafi position is firmly established in the madhhab and remains the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā'): An undivided share in joint property, e.g., a 50% share in a house owned with a partner without physical partition.
يد الاستيفاء (yad al-istīfā'): The hand of recovery; the pawnbroker's right to hold and ultimately seize the pawn to recover the debt.
حبس دائم (habs dā'im): Continuous detention; the requirement that the pawn remain in the murtahin's custody at all times until the debt is paid.
مهاياة (muhāyāh): Time-sharing arrangement; agreeing to use a jointly-owned property in alternating time periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it cannot be sold
B) Because it requires continuous exclusive possession which is impossible in musha'
C) Because the Quran explicitly forbids it
D) Because it leads to uncertainty in the debt amount

Key Takeaway
Pawning an undivided share fails because the Hanafi legal effect of rahn requires exclusive continuous possession, which cannot be achieved with a co-owner, distinguishing rahn from sale and gift.

Rahn al-Musha' from a Partner: Invalid Because Yad al-Istifa' Cannot Be Achieved
Objection and response on the invalidity of rahn musha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rahn al-musha' from a partner and explain why the analogy with hibah is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Core Idea
Rahn al-musha' fails because exclusive possession (yad istifa') cannot be established over an undivided share.

This lesson addresses a common objection: if gifting an undivided share (hibah al-musha') is valid, why can't one pawn it? The Hanafi response is sharp — the two contracts have fundamentally different purposes. Hibah transfers ownership, which can be shared, while rahn requires the creditor to hold the property exclusively. Over a musha', such exclusive holding is impossible, making the contract batil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Objection
First, note that the Hanafi ruling is clear: rahn al-musha' from a partner is impermissible (batil). The objector claims that since hibah of an indivisible musha' is valid, rahn should also be valid. Recognize this as an attempt at analogy.
The objection is not attributed to a specific school but is a common logical challenge.
2
Examine the First Proof: Yad al-Istifa' Cannot Be Established
The passage states that the purpose of rahn is to give the mortgagee the right to hold the pawned item (yad al-istifa'). Over a musha', the mortgagee shares ownership with the pawner, so exclusive possession is impossible. This alone makes the contract invalid.
This proof is derived from the definition of rahn itself; it is not based on a text but on the ma'qul (rational) objective of the contract.
3
Examine the Second Proof: Alternating Possession Creates Contradiction
If a house is held in joint ownership and one partner pawns his share to the other, the mortgagee would one day possess by ownership and another day by rahn. This would mean the pawned item 'exists' only part of the time, which is legally unacceptable.
This proof highlights the practical impossibility of maintaining the pawn continuously.
4
Distinguish Hibah from Rahn (Qiyas Ma'a al-Fariq)
The author responds that the analogy with hibah is false because in hibah, the goal is transfer of ownership, which can be shared. In rahn, the goal is exclusive possession, which cannot be shared. This fundamental difference invalidates the analogy.
The term 'qiyas ma'a al-fariq' means an analogy where the two cases differ in a legally relevant aspect.
5
Recognize the Practical Outcome
The mufta bihi position is that rahn al-musha' from a partner is absolutely invalid. The mortgagee cannot enforce any rights over the undivided share because the essential element of yad istifa' is permanently absent.
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and there is no intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نهیں جب یہ تفصیل ذہن نشیں ہو گئی تو اب سنئے۔ معترض کہتا ہے کہ جب غیر قابل قسمت کا [ہبہ] جائز ہے تو اس کا رہن بھی جائز ہونا چاہیے؟ تو مصنف نے اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ ہبہ کا مقصد اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ موہوب لہ اس کا مالک بن جائے اور ملکیت مشاع کے اوپر بھی ثابت ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ غیر مشاع پر ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور رہن کا حکم ہی اور ہے اور وہ ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور یہ حکم مشاع میں حاصل نہ ہو سکے گا خواہ قابل قسمت ہو یا نہ ہو۔ سوال جب بات یوں ہے کہ ہبہ کا حکم ثبوت ملک ہے تو قابل قسمت کا ہبہ بھی صحیح ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب یہ بھی قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیونکہ قابل قسمت میں واہب قسمت کی مشقت میں پھنسے گا اور غیر قابل قسمت میں یہ بات نہیں۔ فلا اشکال فیہ۔ رہن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں ولا يجوز من شريكه لانه لا يقبل حكمه على الوجه الأول وعلى الوجه الثاني يسكن يوما بحكم الملك ويوما بحكم الرهن فيصير كانه رهن يوما ويوما لا ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہے ( مشاع کا رہن ) اپنے شریک کے ہاتھ اس لئے کہ یہ رہن مشاع رہن کے حکم کو قبول نہیں کرے گا ، وجہ اول کے مطابق اور وجہ ثانی کے مطابق مرتہن اس میں ایک دن رہیگا ملکیت کے اور ایک دن رہن کے حکم سے تو ایسا ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ایک دن رہن کو رکھا اور ایک دن رہن نہیں رکھا۔ تشریح رہن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں ماقبل میں بیان کی گئی ہیں۔ ید استیفاء کا عدم ثبوت جبس دائمی کا استحقاق اب سنئے اگر کسی نے ایسا گھر رہن رکھا جو اس کے اور زید کے درمیان شیوع کے طریقہ پر مشترک ہے اور زید ہی کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے کیونکہ دلیل اول کے مطابق حکم رہن ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وہ یہاں مفقود ہے کیونکہ مشاع پر ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہوتا ہی نہیں ہے۔ اور دلیل ثانی کے مطابق بھی رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جس دائگی مفقود ہے بلکہ یہاں تو صورت یہ ہوگی کہ مرتہن اس میں ایک دن تو اپنی ملک کے لحاظ سے رہے گا اور دوسرے دن رہن کے اعتبار سے گویا کہ ایک دن رہن ہے اور دوسرے دن نہیں ہے اور اس کا عدم جواز ماقبل میں مصرح سے لہذا شریک کے ہاتھ ہی مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہے۔
No, when this detail is understood, now listen. The objector says: When hibah of an indivisible thing is valid, why should its rahn not be valid? The author replied: This is false analogy because the purpose and ruling of hibah is that the donee becomes owner, and ownership is established over a musha' as over non-musha'. But the ruling of rahn is different: it is the establishment of yad al-istifa', and this ruling cannot be realized in musha', whether it is divisible or not. Question: If so, then hibah of a divisible musha' should also be valid? Answer: This is also false analogy because in divisible musha', the donor will be trapped in the hardship of division, while in indivisible musha' this is not the case. So there is no problem. Two proofs for the impermissibility of rahn musha': 'And it is not valid from his partner because it does not accept its ruling according to the first aspect, and according to the second aspect he resides one day by the ruling of ownership and one day by the ruling of rahn, so it becomes as if he had rahn one day and not rahn another day.' Translation: And it is not valid (rahn musha') from his partner because this rahn musha' will not accept the ruling of rahn, according to the first reason, and according to the second reason the mortgagee will reside in it one day by ownership and one day by rahn, so it becomes as if he kept rahn one day and not rahn another day. Commentary: Two proofs for impermissibility of rahn musha' were mentioned previously. Non-establishment of yad istifa'. Now listen: if someone pawns a house that is shared between him and Zaid in a common way, and pawns it to Zaid himself, this is also invalid because according to the first proof, the ruling of rahn is establishment of yad istifa', and that is absent here because yad istifa' is never established over musha'. And according to the second proof, rahn will not be valid because the mortgagee will reside one day by his ownership and another day by rahn, as if rahn exists one day and not another, and its impermissibility is clear from the previous. Therefore, rahn musha' from a partner is not valid.

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of pawning an undivided share (rahn al-musha') to a partner. The author begins by addressing an objection: if gifting (hibah) an indivisible musha' is valid, then pawning it should also be valid. The response is that this is a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). In hibah, the goal is transfer of ownership, and ownership can be established over a musha'. In rahn, the goal is establishment of the right of retention (yad al-istifa') for the creditor, which cannot be realized over a musha' because the creditor cannot physically possess the entire property to the exclusion of others. The second objection about hibah of a divisible musha' is also refuted because division would burden the donor. The passage then gives two textual proofs from the matn: first, that musha' does not admit the ruling of rahn (lack of mahalliyyah), and second, that possession would alternate between ownership and rahn, leading to a contradiction. The commentary explains these proofs in detail, emphasizing that the first proof (regarding yad istifa') is fundamental, and the second shows that such a contract would lead to instability. The conclusion is that rahn musha' from a partner is absolutely invalid.

Key Terms
رهن مشاع (rahn al-musha'): Pawning an undivided share of a jointly owned property
ید استیفاء (yad al-istifa'): The right of the mortgagee to hold the pawned property until the debt is paid
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that fails due to a fundamental difference between the two cases

Rahn al-musha' from a partner is batil because the mortgagee cannot achieve exclusive possession (yad istifa') over an undivided share.

Subsequent Co-ownership and Its Effect on a Mortgage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shuyu' tari' and rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of subsequent co-ownership (shuyu' tari') on a pre-existing mortgage and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Subsequent co-ownership invalidates a mortgage under al-Mabsut, but Abu Yusuf allows continuity.

When a mortgaged property later becomes co-owned, does the mortgage remain valid? The Hanafi school presents two views. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between the narration of al-Mabsut (Imam Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf, focusing on the key concept of mahalliyyah (suitability) and the distinction between initiation and continuity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Recognize that the issue is whether subsequent co-ownership (shuyu' tari') invalidates a pre-existing mortgage. The two positions within the Hanafi school are: (1) from al-Mabsut: it invalidates; (2) from Imam Abu Yusuf: it does not invalidate.
The shuyu' tari' differs from initial shuyu' (present at contract formation).
2
Understand the proof for al-Mabsut
Al-Mabsut argues that musha' (co-owned property) lacks mahalliyyah (suitability) to be the subject of a mortgage. This deficiency applies equally to initiation and continuity, so even subsequent co-ownership destroys the mahalliyyah, invalidating the mortgage.
Analogy with marriage: marrying a mahram is invalid both at initiation and continuity.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the ruling for continuity (baqa') is more lenient than for initiation (ibtida'). The difficulty of taking possession (qabd) at initiation is not present during continuity. He draws an analogy with hibah (gift), where subsequent co-ownership does not invalidate the gift.
In hibah, musha' can be validly owned, and possession at initiation is only to avoid liability.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a mortgaged property becomes co-owned after the contract, according to al-Mabsut the mortgage becomes fasid (invalid), while according to Abu Yusuf it remains valid.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of al-Mabsut, though both views are recognized.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text suggests that the stronger view is from al-Mabsut, as it is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by a detailed proof. Abu Yusuf's view is considered a solitary narration.
In practice, a mortgage becomes invalid when subsequent co-ownership is established.

والشيوع الطاري يمنع بقاء الرهن في رواية الأصل وعن ابي يوسف انه لا يمنع لان حكم البقاء اسهل من حكم الابتداء فاشبه الهبة ترجمہ اور شیوع طاری مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق بقاء رہن کو روکتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ نہیں روکتا اس لئے کہ بقاء کا حکم ابتداء کے حکم سے آسان ہے تو یہ ہبہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح کسی نے کوئی مکان رہن رکھا بعد میں زید نے اس میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کیا اور کہا کہ اس کا غیر معین اتنا حصہ میرا ہے تو اب ہوگا ؟ کیونکہ اب اس میں شیوع آ گیا اور اس کو شیوع طاری کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ پہلے سے ظاہر نہیں بلکہ اس کا ظہور اب ہو رہا ہے تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ا مبسوط کی روایت کہ رہن فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ شیوع ابتدائی ہو یا طاری وہ منافی جواز رہین ہے ۔ ۲ روایت امام ابو یوسف کہ یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ بقاء رہن کی حالت ہے نہ کہ ابتدا ء بہن کی اور حالت بقاء میں ابتداء کے مقابلہ میں کچھ آسانی اور تخفیف ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ جائز ہے اور رہن فاسد نہ ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے سبہ میں یہ صورت پیش آ جائے تو ہبہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا لہذا ر ہن بھی فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ پہلی دلیل وجه الاول ان الامتناع لعدم المحلية وما يرجع اليه فالابتداء والبقاء سواء كالمحرمية في باب النكاح بخلاف الهبة لان المشاع يقبل حكمها وهو الملك و اعتبار القبض في الابتداء لنفى الغرامة على مابيناه ولا حاجة الى اعتباره فى حالة البقاء ولهذا يصح الرجوع فى بعض الهبة ولا يجوز فسخ العقد في بعض الرهن ترجمہ اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ( رہن مشاع کا ) ممنوع ہو نا محلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور جو کل کی جانب راجع ہے تو ابتدا ، اور بقا ء برابر ہیں جیسے باب نکاح میں محرمیت بخلاف ہبہ کے اس لئے کہ مشاع ہبہ کے حکم کو قبول کر لیتا ہے اور وہ حکم ملک ہے اور ابتداء میں قبضہ کا اعتبار تاوان کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور حالت بقا میں قبضہ کے اعتبار کرنے کی کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ہبہ کے بعض حصہ میں رجوع جائز ہے اور مرہون کے بعض حصہ میں عقد رہن کا فسح جائز نہیں ہے۔ تشریح مصنف یہاں سے مبسوط کی روایت کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مشاع میں یہ صلاحیت ہی نہیں کہ رہن کا محل بن سکے اور جس چیز میں محلیت ہی معدوم ہوتی ہے اس میں ابتداء اور بقاء دونوں برابر ہوا کرتی ہے۔ جیسے مثلا اپنی رضاعی بہن سے نکاح حرام ہے کیونکہ وہ نکات کا محل ہی نہیں ہے لیکن اگر لاعلمی میں نکاح کر لیا اور بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ سی تو اس کی رضاعی بہن ہے تو فورا تفریق واجب ہوگی ابتداء اور بقاء میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کیونکہ محل نکاح مفقود ہے ایسے ہی یہاں محل رہن مفقود ہے لہذا ابتداء اور بقاء دونوں صورتوں کا ایک ہی حکم ہوگا یعنی عدم جواز ۔ سوال اگر زید نے خالد کو کوئی مکان ہبہ کر دیا اور بعد میں بکر نے اس مکان میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر دیا تو ہبہ بھی باطل ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ ہبہ باطل نہیں ہے؟
And subsequent co-ownership prevents the continuity of rahn according to the narration of al-Mabsut, and from Abu Yusuf that it does not prevent because the ruling of continuity is easier than the ruling of commencement, so it resembles hibah. Translation: And shuyu' tari' according to the narration of al-Mabsut prevents the continuity of rahn, and from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it does not prevent because the ruling of continuity is easier than the ruling of commencement, so it becomes similar to hibah. Commentary: Someone pawned a house; later Zaid proved his right in it and said that an unspecified portion of it is mine. So what happens? Because now shuyu' has entered, and this is called shuyu' tari' because it was not apparent before but now appears. There are two narrations: 1. Narration of al-Mabsut: rahn becomes invalid because shuyu', whether initial or subsequent, is contrary to the permissibility of rahn. 2. Narration of Imam Abu Yusuf: it is valid because this is a state of continuity of rahn, not initiation, and in the state of continuity there is some ease and leniency compared to initiation, so it is valid and rahn will not become invalid. And this is like in hibah when such a situation occurs, hibah does not become invalid, so rahn also will not become invalid. The first proof: 'The first aspect is that the prohibition is due to lack of mahalliyyah (suitability), and what is dependent on it, initiation and continuity are equal, like mahramiyyah in the chapter of marriage, unlike hibah because musha' accepts its ruling, which is ownership, and the consideration of possession (qabd) in initiation is to remove the liability (gharamah) as we have explained, and there is no need to consider it in the state of continuity. For this reason, revocation in part of a hibah is valid, but rescission of the contract in part of a pawned item is not valid.' Translation of the first proof: The proof for the first (narration of al-Mabsut) is that prohibition is due to lack of mahalliyyah, and what depends on it, initiation and continuity are equal, like mahramiyyah in marriage, unlike hibah because musha' accepts its ruling, i.e., ownership, and the consideration of possession at initiation is to remove liability as we have explained, and there is no need to consider it in the state of continuity. For this reason, revocation in part of hibah is valid, but rescission of the rahn contract in part of the pawned item is not valid. Commentary: The author here gives the proof for the narration of al-Mabsut. The summary is that musha' lacks the capacity to be a subject of rahn, and when mahalliyyah is absent, initiation and continuity are equal. For example, marrying one's foster sister is prohibited because she is not a valid subject for marriage; if one marries unknowingly and later discovers she is a foster sister, separation is obligatory immediately, with no difference between initiation and continuity because the subject of marriage is absent. Similarly, here the subject of rahn is absent, so both initiation and continuity have the same ruling: impermissibility. Question: If Zaid gifts a house to Khalid, and later Bakr proves his right in that house, should the hibah also become invalid, whereas the hibah is not invalid?
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of subsequent co-ownership (shuyu' tari') on a pre-existing mortgage contract. The author presents two views within the Hanafi school. The first view, recorded in al-Mabsut (the leading narration from Imam Muhammad), holds that shuyu' tari' invalidates the mortgage because the property becomes partially owned by another, and a mortgage over a musha' is fundamentally invalid due to the lack of mahalliyyah (suitability). The second view, attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, states that the mortgage remains valid because continuity (baqa') is easier than initiation (ibtida'), and the contract should not be disturbed. The commentary explains the reasoning: in cases of absolute mahalliyyah absence (like marriage with a mahram), initiation and continuity are equal; but in rahn, the prohibition is due to lack of mahalliyyah, so even subsequent occurrence should nullify. However, Abu Yusuf argues that the difficulty of taking possession at initiation is absent during continuity, and he draws an analogy with hibah, where subsequent co-ownership does not invalidate the gift. The author then presents the detailed proof for the al-Mabsut view: the prohibition of rahn musha' is because musha' cannot be a valid subject (mahall) for rahn, and this deficiency affects both initiation and continuity equally. This is contrasted with hibah, where musha' can be owned and the possession requirement at initiation is only to avoid liability, which is not required during continuity. The passage ends with a question comparing hibah, inviting reflection on the difference.

Key Terms
شیوع طاری (shuyu' tari'): Co-ownership that arises after the contract, not present at initiation
محلیت (mahalliyyah): The suitability of a property to be the subject of a contract
بقاء (baqa'): Continuation of a contract after its valid initiation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration of al-Mabsut, why does shuyu' tari' invalidate a pre-existing rahn?
A) Because the contract becomes usurious
B) Because musha' lacks mahalliyyah for rahn, which applies equally to initiation and continuity
C) Because the mortgagee must always have exclusive possession
D) Because the debtor's ownership becomes uncertain

Key Takeaway
Subsequent co-ownership (shuyu' tari') invalidates a pre-existing mortgage according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-Mabsut), due to the absence of mahalliyyah.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate

Supervening Undivided Share in Rahn: Two Hanafi Narrations
Explains two Hanafi narrations on whether a supervening undivided share invalidates an existing pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of a supervening undivided share (shuyu' tari') on a pledge (rahn) and explain the proof for each position.

Core Idea
A supervening undivided share invalidates a pledge according to al-Mabsut, but Abu Yusuf holds it remains valid due to the leniency of continuity.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a third party’s claim to a share in pledged property after the contract invalidates the pledge. Two narrations are presented: one from al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah) declaring the pledge fasid, and another from Imam Abu Yusuf declaring it valid. Understanding the reasoning behind each position deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists apply qiyas and istihsan in the law of pledges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Understand what shuyu' tari' (supervening undivided share) is and how it arises in the context of rahn. In the scenario, after a house is pledged, a third party proves ownership of an unspecified share.
2
State each Hanafi position
The first position (al-Mabsut) says the pledge becomes fasid. The second (Abu Yusuf) says it remains valid.
3
Analyze al-Mabsut's proof
The proof is that an undivided share lacks mahalliyyah (capacity to be a valid subject) for rahn, and this incapacity applies equally to initiation and continuity, analogous to the prohibition of marrying a foster sister.
The author uses qiyas to mahramiyyah in nikah.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the rules of continuity (bagha') are lighter than initiation. He analogizes to hibah, where a supervening share does not invalidate the gift because the ruling (ownership) still exists.
He uses istihsan based on this analogy.
5
Compare and determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that under al-Mabsut's view, the pledge is void and a new contract is needed; under Abu Yusuf's view, the pledge remains valid and the creditor retains rights over the debtor's share.
The text does not give a definitive tarjih, but the first narration is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

ترجمہ اور شیوع طاری مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق بقاء رہن کو روکتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ نہیں روکتا اس لئے کہ بقاء کا حکم ابتداء کے حکم سے آسان ہے تو یہ ہبہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔
تشریح کسی نے کوئی مکان رہن رکھا بعد میں زید نے اس میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کیا اور کہا کہ اس کا غیر معین اتنا حصہ میرا ہے تو اب کیا ہوگا؟ کیونکہ اب اس میں شیوع آ گیا اور اس کو شیوع طاری کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ پہلے سے ظاہر نہیں بلکہ اس کا ظہور اب ہو رہا ہے تو اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔
۱ مبسوط کی روایت کہ رہن فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ شیوع ابتدائی ہو یا طاری وہ منافی جواز رہن ہے۔ ۲ روایت امام ابو یوسف کہ یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ بقاء رہن کی حالت ہے نہ کہ ابتداء رہن کی اور حالت بقاء میں ابتداء کے مقابلہ میں کچھ آسانی اور تخفیف ہوتی ہے لہذا یہ جائز ہے اور رہن فاسد نہ ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے ہبہ میں یہ صورت پیش آ جائے تو ہبہ فاسد نہیں ہوتا لہذا رہن بھی فاسد نہ ہوگا۔
پہلی دلیل
وجه الاول ان الامتناع لعدم المحلية وما يرجع اليه فالابتداء والبقاء سواء كالمحرمية في باب النكاح بخلاف الهبة لان المشاع يقبل حكمها وهو الملك و اعتبار القبض في الابتداء لنفى الغرامة على مابيناه ولا حاجة الى اعتباره فى حالة البقاء ولهذا يصح الرجوع فى بعض الهبة ولا يجوز فسخ العقد في بعض الرهن
ترجمہ اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ (رہن مشاع کا) ممنوع ہونا محلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور جو کل کی جانب راجع ہے تو ابتدا اور بقا برابر ہیں جیسے باب نکاح میں محرمیت بخلاف ہبہ کے اس لئے کہ مشاع ہبہ کے حکم کو قبول کر لیتا ہے اور وہ حکم ملک ہے اور ابتداء میں قبضہ کا اعتبار تاوان کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور حالت بقا میں قبضہ کے اعتبار کرنے کی کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ہبہ کے بعض حصہ میں رجوع جائز ہے اور مرہون کے بعض حصہ میں عقد رہن کا فسخ جائز نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مصنف یہاں سے مبسوط کی روایت کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مشاع میں یہ صلاحیت ہی نہیں کہ رہن کا محل بن سکے اور جس چیز میں محلیت ہی معدوم ہوتی ہے اس میں ابتداء اور بقاء دونوں برابر ہوا کرتی ہے۔ جیسے مثلا اپنی رضاعی بہن سے نکاح حرام ہے کیونکہ وہ نکاح کا محل ہی نہیں ہے لیکن اگر لاعلمی میں نکاح کر لیا اور بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ اس کی رضاعی بہن ہے تو فورا تفریق واجب ہوگی ابتداء اور بقاء میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے کیونکہ محل نکاح مفقود ہے ایسے ہی یہاں محل رہن مفقود ہے لہذا ابتداء اور بقاء دونوں صورتوں کا ایک ہی حکم ہوگا یعنی عدم جواز۔
سوال اگر زید نے خالد کو کوئی مکان ہبہ کر دیا اور بعد میں بکر نے اس مکان میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر دیا تو ہبہ بھی باطل ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ ہبہ باطل نہیں ہے؟
جواب ہبہ باطل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ جواز ہبہ کا مدار اس پر ہے کہ حکم ہبہ کا وجود ہو سکے اور وہ ملکیت ہے جو موجود ہے اس لئے ہبہ جائز ہے۔
سوال جب آپ نے حکم ہبہ کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ہبہ کو باطل نہیں کہا تو آپ کو چاہیے کہ قابل قسمت چیز کا ابتداء ہبہ بھی آپ کے نزدیک جائز ہو کیونکہ ملک کا وجود وہاں بھی ہو جائے گا حالانکہ آپ اس کو جائز نہیں کہتے؟
جواب ماقبل میں ہم بتا چکے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں واہب پر قسمت کا تاوان خواہ مخواہ لازم آئے گا حالانکہ اس نے اس کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے اس وجہ سے صورت مذکورہ میں ابتدائی ہبہ کو ملک کے موجود ہو سکنے کے باوجود جائز قرار نہیں دیا گیا اور حالت بقاء میں قبضہ کا اعتبار کرنے کی کوئی حاجت نہیں رہی کیونکہ قبضہ تو تمامیت عقد کی وجہ سے لازم ہوا کرتا ہے اور یہاں عقد پہلے سے تام ہو چکا ہے۔
سوال کیا آپ ایسی کچھ جزئیات پیش کر سکتے ہیں جو مسئلہ مذکورہ کی مؤید ہوں؟
جواب جی ہاں کر سکتے ہیں۔ سنئے
-1 زید نے خالد کو اپنا مکان ہبہ کیا پھر غیر معین کچھ حصہ کو واپس لے لیا تو ہبہ باطل نہیں کیونکہ یہ شیوع طاری ہے جو ہبہ کیلئے مضر نہیں ہے۔
-2 زید نے خالد کے ہاتھ اپنا مکان رہن رکھا پھر ان دونوں نے مکان مرہون کے غیر معین حصہ کو عقد رہن سے خارج کر دیا تو یہ جائز نہیں بلکہ عقد رہن باطل ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ یہ شیوع طاری ہے جو رہن کو فاسد کر دینے والا ہے۔
Translation: And according to the narration of al-Mabsut, supervening shuyu' prevents the continuation of the pledge, and it is transmitted from Abu Yusuf that it does not prevent, because the ruling of continuity is easier than the ruling of initiation, so it resembles hibah. Commentary: Someone pledged a house, later Zayd proved his right in it and said an unspecified share is mine, so what happens? Because shuyu' has arisen, called supervening shuyu' since it was not apparent before. There are two narrations: 1. Narration of al-Mabsut: the pledge becomes fasid because shuyu', whether initial or supervening, is contrary to validity of pledge. 2. Narration of Imam Abu Yusuf: it is valid because this is a state of continuity of the pledge, not initiation, and in continuity there is some ease and leniency compared to initiation, so it is valid and the pledge does not become fasid, and it becomes like the case in hibah – if this situation occurs in hibah, hibah does not become fasid. First proof: The text of the first proof in Arabic: 'The first reason is that the prohibition is due to lack of capacity (mahalliyyah), and in that which is referred back to, initiation and continuity are equal, like mahramiyyah in the chapter of nikah, unlike hibah because the undivided share accepts its ruling, which is ownership, and the consideration of possession in initiation is to avoid liability as we explained, and there is no need to consider it in the state of continuity, and for this reason revocation of a part of hibah is valid, but annulment of the contract in a part of the pledge is not valid.' Commentary: The author is giving the proof of the al-Mabsut narration: an undivided share lacks capacity to be a valid subject of pledge, and when capacity is absent, initiation and continuity are equal. For example, marrying one's foster sister is unlawful because she is not a valid subject of marriage; if one marries unknowingly and later discovers, separation is obligatory immediately – no difference between initiation and continuity. Similarly here, the subject of pledge is lacking, so the same ruling applies in both cases: impermissibility. Question: If Zayd gave Khalid a house as hibah, and later Bakr proved his right in that house, should the hibah also become invalid? Yet it does not. Answer: The hibah is not invalid because its validity depends on the existence of the ruling of hibah, which is ownership, and that exists. Question: If you do not declare hibah invalid due to existence of ownership, then you should also allow the initial hibah of a divisible item because ownership exists there too, but you do not allow it? Answer: Earlier we explained that in that case, the donor inevitably incurs the liability of division, which he did not undertake, so initial hibah is not allowed despite existence of ownership. In the state of continuity, there is no need to consider possession because possession is necessitated by the completion of the contract, and here the contract is already complete. Question: Can you provide some examples that support this matter? Answer: Yes, listen: 1. Zayd gave his house to Khalid as hibah, then took back an unspecified part – the hibah is not invalid because this is supervening shuyu', which does not harm hibah. 2. Zayd pledged his house to Khalid, then both of them excluded an unspecified part of the pledged house from the pledge contract – this is not valid; rather the pledge contract becomes invalid, because this is supervening shuyu', which invalidates the pledge.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a third party's claim to an undivided share (shuyu' tari') in property that was already pledged. Two positions are presented. The first, from the Zahir al-Riwayah via al-Mabsut, holds that the pledge becomes fasid because an undivided share lacks the capacity (mahalliyyah) to be the subject of a pledge, and this incapacity applies equally to the initiation and continuation of the contract. The proof uses qiyas to the case of marriage with a foster sister: just as such a marriage is invalid from the start and must be annulled immediately upon discovery, so too a pledge affected by shuyu' becomes invalid retroactively. The second position, attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf, holds that the pledge remains valid because the state of continuity (bagha') is governed by more lenient rules than initiation. The proof relies on istihsan, citing the analogy of hibah: if a third party claims a share in a gifted property, the hibah does not become invalid because the ruling of hibah (ownership) still exists. The author then reconciles the difference by noting that in hibah, possession is required only at initiation to avoid liability, not for continuity, whereas in rahn, the requirement of possession is integral to the contract. Two examples are provided to illustrate the practical consequence: returning a part of a gift does not invalidate it, but excluding a part of a pledged property invalidates the pledge.

Key Terms
شیوع طاری (shuyu' tari'): A supervening undivided share – a claim of partial ownership that arises after the contract has been concluded, not present at the time of contracting.
محلیت (mahalliyyah): Capacity of a property to serve as a valid subject (mahall) of a contract. If a property lacks mahalliyyah, the contract is invalid.
رہن (rahn): A contract of pledge where property is given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration of al-Mabsut in the text, what is the effect of a supervening undivided share (shuyu' tari') on a pledge (rahn)?
A) The pledge remains valid.
B) The pledge becomes fasid (invalid).
C) The pledge becomes voidable at the option of the creditor.
D) The pledge becomes suspended until the claim is resolved.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a supervening undivided share renders a pledge invalid according to the dominant narration (al-Mabsut), but Imam Abu Yusuf allows its validity under the principle of continuity being easier than initiation.

The Rule of Pledging Attached Items
States the general rule that one cannot pledge something attached to something not pledged.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule regarding pledging items attached to unpledged property and apply it to new cases by identifying when separate possession is impossible.

Core Idea
A pledge is invalid if the pledged item is physically attached to something not pledged, because separate possession is impossible.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: the invalidity of pledging an item that is naturally attached to something not included in the pledge. The reason lies in the Hanafi condition that the creditor must be able to take exclusive possession (qabd) of the pledged item alone. We will explore the examples given and understand the underlying legal maxim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the text: what is the ruling on pledging fruit on trees without the trees? The text says 'la yajuz' (it is not valid).
The ruling is a clear prohibition of such a pledge.
2
Identify the 'illah (reason)
Why is it not valid? Because the fruit is naturally attached (mutasil) to the tree, which is not part of the pledge. This attachment makes separate possession impossible.
The 'illah is the prevention of exclusive qabd.
3
Understand the analogy to shuyu'
The text compares this to an undivided share (shuyu') because the pledged item is mixed with an unpledged item in a way that prevents separation.
Like a share in a jointly-owned property, separate possession is not possible without the co-owner's consent.
4
Extract the general maxim
The text concludes with a universal rule: whenever the pledged item is attached to something not pledged, the pledge is invalid. This is a qa'idah kulliyyah.
This maxim governs many subsidiary cases.
5
Apply to the given examples
The text gives three examples: fruit on trees, crops in ground, trees on land. Verify that each fits the maxim.
Each example illustrates the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
